1 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Calik v. Kongable


Supreme Court No. CV-98-0389-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


195 Ariz. 496; 990 P.2d 1055; 1999 Ariz. LEXIS 123; 316 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 26



December 20, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Court of Appeals No. 1 CA-SA 97-0273. Yuma County No. SC97C00059. Special Action from the Superior Court in Yuma County. The Honorable Kirby Kongable, Judge. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One. 194 Ariz. 188, 979 P.2d 1 (1998).



DISPOSITION: Special Action from the Superior Court in Yuma County VACATED AND REMANDED. Opinion of the Court of Court of Appeals, Division One VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal by petitioner from the Court of Appeals Yuma County (Arizona) in a criminal case involving Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-901.01 and issues of incarceration and probation for possession of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner pleaded guilty to possession of methamphetamine weighing less than nine grams, a class four felony. The trial judge concluded that because he was a first-time offender, he was to be sentenced under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-901.01. The judge also determined he could incarcerate petitioner in the county jail as a condition of probation. Petitioner objected, arguing that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-901.01 prohibited the judge from imposing such a condition. The Supreme Court granted review to determine whether Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-901.01 prohibited a trial court from imposing jail time as a condition of probation for a person convicted of first-offense personal possession or use of a controlled substance. It stated that incarceration may not be imposed under such circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the decision of the lower court and remanded the case stating that neither the text nor the intent of the statute supported imposing incarceration as a condition of the required probation for first-time offenders.

 

2 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Randolph v. Groscost


Supreme Court No. CV-99-0054-SA


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


195 Ariz. 423; 989 P.2d 751; 1999 Ariz. LEXIS 124; 316 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 40



December 17, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Special Action filed in the Supreme Court.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners filed writ of mandamus, claiming that Arizona legislators were obligated to enforce the per diem provision of proposition that was adopted by Arizona's electorate.


OVERVIEW: Arizona's electorate approved a proposition that both raised legislative salaries and sought to change the method for setting legislators' per diem reimbursements. Arizona's Attorney General concluded that salary provision was valid but that the per diem recommendation exceeded the authority of Arizona's Commission on Salaries for Elective State Officers (Commission). Petitioners filed writ of mandamus, claiming that the Arizona legislature was obligated to enforce the per diem provision of the proposition. The court held that because the Commission's authority was limited to recommending changes in legislative salaries, and because per diem reimbursement was not a salary, the Commission lacked authority to recommend changes in the legislative per diem rate. The court held that the salary increase provision of the proposition could operate independently of the per diem provision. The court declared the per diem provision invalid, severed the per diem provision, and upheld the salary provision.


OUTCOME: Court denied petitioners' writ of mandamus, holding that state commission exceeded its authority when it sought to change the method for setting legislators' per diem reimbursement.

 

3 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Cronin v. Sheldon


Supreme Court No. CV-98-0495-SA and Supreme Court No. CV-08-0580-SA (Consolidated)


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


195 Ariz. 531; 991 P.2d 231; 1999 Ariz. LEXIS 125; 314 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3; 15 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1345; 81 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 822; 139 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P58,800



December 17, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 23, 1999. Second Correction March 3, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Special Action from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Steven D. Sheldon, Judge (Cronin). The Honorable John H. Seidel, Judge (Finley). Maricopa County No. CV 98-08453 and Maricopa County No. CV-98-12454.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In Maricopa County Superior Court (Ariz.), petitioners brought separate actions for wrongful discharge against defendant employers, who argued that the Employment Protection Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1501(3)(b)(i) (supp. 1998), barred the claims. The trial courts agreed with defendants, but the Supreme Court of Arizona granted a petition for special action and motion to consolidate petitioners' claims.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners filed separate actions for wrongful discharge against defendant employers, which argued that the exclusive remedies provision of Employment Protection Act (EPA), Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1501(3)(b)(i) (supp. 1998), barred such claims. The trial judges entered judgments for defendants, but the Supreme Court of Arizona granted a petition for special action and motion to consolidate petitioners' claims. The issue presented was whether claims alleging the tort of wrongful termination in violation of public policy in the Arizona Civil Rights Act (ACRA), Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 41-1401 to -1492 (1999), could be constitutionally restricted to the ACRA's statutory remedies by EPA. The court affirmed, holding that the preamble to the EPA, though unconstitutional on its face, did not implicate the constitutionality of the statutory text; the EPA's exclusive remedies provision restricting tort claims under the ACRA violated neither the anti-abrogation clause nor non-limitation clauses of the Arizona constitution; petitioners lacked standing to assert a claim that EPA violated the equal privileges clause and failed to demonstrate the applicability of impairment of the contracts clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that the unconstitutional preamble to Employment Protection Act (EPA) did not implicate the constitutionality of the statutory text; that EPA's exclusive remedies provision restricting tort claims under Arizona Civil Rights Act did not violate the anti-abrogation or non-limitation clauses of the Arizona constitution; and that the petitioners lacked standing to assert that the EPA violated the equal privileges clause.

 

4 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


In re GENERAL ADJUDICATION OF ALL RIGHTS


Supreme Court Nos. WC-90-0001-IR, WC-90-0002-IR, WC-90-0003-IR, WC-90-0004-IR, WC-90-0005-IR, WC-90-0006-IR, WC-90-0007-IR (Consolidated) & WC-79-0001, WC-79-0002, WC-79-0003, WC-79-0004 (Consolidated)


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


195 Ariz. 411; 989 P.2d 739; 1999 Ariz. LEXIS 116



November 19, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied June 19, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 4290.
Writ of certiorari denied, Motion granted by Phelps Dodge Corp. v. United States, 530 U.S. 1250, 120 S. Ct. 2705, 147 L. Ed. 2d 974, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 4290 (2000)
Writ of certiorari denied, Motion granted by Salt River Valley Water Users' Ass'n v. United States, 530 U.S. 1250, 120 S. Ct. 2705, 147 L. Ed. 2d 974, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 4291 (2000)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Maricopa County Nos. W-1, W-2, W-3, W-4 (Consolidated). Interlocutory Review of September 30, 1988 Order Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Stanley Z. Goodfarb, Judge (retired).
In re General Adjudication of All Rights to Use Water in the Gila River Sys. & Source, 171 Ariz. 230, 830 P.2d 442, 1992 Ariz. LEXIS 25 (Ariz., 1992)



DISPOSITION: QUESTIONS ANSWERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In comprehensive general stream adjudication, various parties filed petitions for interlocutory review of order of the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) regarding a number of questions concerning the relationship of groundwater and surface water.


OVERVIEW: In comprehensive general stream adjudication, various parties filed petitions for interlocutory review of the trial court's order regarding a number of questions concerning the relationship of groundwater and surface water. The instant action addressed two of six issues previously outlined by the court. The court concluded that if the United States implicitly intended, when it established reservations, to reserve sufficient unappropriated water to meet the reservations' needs, it must have intended that reservation of water to come from whatever particular sources each reservation had at hand. Thus, federal reserved rights applied to groundwater. The court further held that it could not defer to state law, the "reasonable use" doctrine, where to do so would defeat federal water rights. Thus, the court held that holders of federal reserved rights enjoy greater protection from groundwater pumping than do holders of state law rights to the extent necessary to accomplish purpose of reservation.


OUTCOME: Questions answered as follows: Federal reserved rights extended to groundwater to extent groundwater necessary to accomplish purpose of reservation; and holders of federal reserved rights enjoy greater protection from groundwater pumping than do holders of state law rights to the extent necessary to accomplish purpose of reservation.

 

5 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Van Adams


Supreme Court No. CR-97-0471-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


194 Ariz. 408; 984 P.2d 16; 1999 Ariz. LEXIS 89; 306 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 22



June 18, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied February 22, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1286.
Writ of certiorari denied Van Adams v. Arizona, 528 U.S. 1172, 120 S. Ct. 1199, 145 L. Ed. 2d 1102, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1286 (2000)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Claim dismissed by, Motion denied by Van Adams v. Schriro, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 24934 (D. Ariz., Mar. 30, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Maricopa County Superior Court No. CR-96-02618. Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. The Honorable Ronald S. Reinstein, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted him of first-degree premeditated murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was proved to have approached his victim, a lady who worked alone as a real estate salesperson, and shown interest in a purchase. The victim's body was later found with semen stains and evidence of asphyxiation. Appellant was the last prospective buyer that was noticed and sighted by witnesses, and he was thereafter seen with facial injury. Appellant had been convicted of a similar offense. He was convicted of first-degree premeditated murder and sentenced to death. On appeal, he contended that the trial court should have instructed the jury on the lesser-included offense of second-degree murder and should not have admitted evidence of other crimes. He also contended that the death penalty was per se cruel and unusual punishment. The court asserted that a trial court was not required to instruct on a lesser offense that was unsupported by evidence. The court determined that the evidence of prior act was only admitted to prove appellant's motive, knowledge, and absence of mistake. Finally, the court rejected the argument that the death penalty was a cruel and unusual punishment. It affirmed the conviction and sentence.


OUTCOME: The order that convicted appellant of first-degree premeditated murder and sentenced him to death was affirmed because the trial court was not required to instruct on a lesser offense that was unsupported by evidence. The court further held that the death penalty was not a cruel and unusual punishment.

 

6 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. White


Supreme Court No. CR-96-0716-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


194 Ariz. 344; 982 P.2d 819; 1999 Ariz. LEXIS 80; 2697 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 29



June 10, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied March 6, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1778. As Amended.
Writ of certiorari denied White v. Arizona, 529 U.S. 1005, 120 S. Ct. 1272, 146 L. Ed. 2d 221, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1778 (2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Yavapai County. The Honorable James Hancock, Judge. Yavapai County No. CR-12855.
State v. White, 168 Ariz. 500, 815 P.2d 869, 1991 Ariz. LEXIS 57 (Ariz., 1991)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Yavapai County (Arizona), which rejected appellant's nonstatutory mitigating factors and found pecuniary gain as an aggravating factor under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-703(F)(5), in appellant's sentencing hearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first degree murder and was sentenced to death. In the sentencing hearing, the trial court found pecuniary gain as an aggravating factor under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-703(F)(5). Upon resentencing, appellant urged nonstatutory mitigating factors in his defense, but the trial court held that they were insufficient to overcome the substantial weight of contrary evidence that the murder was motivated by the expectation of pecuniary gain. On appeal, appellant contended that the trial court erred in failing to accept as a nonstatutory mitigating factor the prosecutor's belief that the death penalty was inappropriate. The court held that a recommendation of leniency from authorities that were intimately involved in a case carried significant weight and may constitute a mitigating circumstance. In weighing the opinions of the prosecutors, the court found that they were easily outdistanced by the premeditated scheme to murder the victim. The opinions were insufficient to warrant a change in appellant's sentence under § 13-703.01.The court went on the reject the rest of appellant's nonstatutory mitigating factors and affirmed his sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's death sentence on the basis that the aggravating factor of an expectation of pecuniary gain outweighed appellant's nonstatutory mitigating factors.

 

7 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Napolitano v. Brown


Supreme Court No. CV-98-0547-SA.


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


194 Ariz. 340; 982 P.2d 815; 1999 Ariz. LEXIS 77; 297 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 5



June 4, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition granted by State v. Miles, 2017 Ariz. LEXIS 230 (Ariz., Aug. 30, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Special Action from the Superior Court of Pima County. The Honorable Michael Brown, Judge. Pima County No. CR-40238.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of the order of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which found that legislative amendments to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4234.D, .F (1998) were unconstitutional because the amendments conflicted with time limits for requesting post-conviction relief established in Ariz. R. Crim. P. 32.4.c.


OVERVIEW: Respondent trial court granted the real party in interest death row inmate's motion that amendments to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4234.D, .F (1998) were unconstitutional because they impermissibly conflicted with post-conviction relief time limits in capital cases under Ariz. R. Crim. P. 32.4.c. Petitioner state sought review and alleged that the amendments were constitutional because they were enacted pursuant to the Victim's Bill of Rights (VBR), Ariz. Const. art. II, § 2.1, which permitted the legislature to enact rules to assure victims' rights to speedy trials. The court affirmed and held that the amendments violated the separation of powers doctrine. Courts had the exclusive power to make procedural rules. There was no evidence that the amendments were enacted pursuant to the VBR. The legislative history revealed that the amendments were enacted to comply with a federal statute. The amendments did not apply equally to non-capital cases. Petitioner's procedural rulemaking power extended only to procedural rules concerning victims. The VBR did not create a speedy trial right that was unique to victims. The court was able to sever the unconstitutional provisions from the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that amendments to a state statute were unconstitutional and held that that petitioner's amendments of statutory time limits for post-conviction relief in capital cases violated the separation of powers doctrine.

 

8 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wagner


Supreme Court No. CR-98-0481-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


194 Ariz. 310; 982 P.2d 270; 1999 Ariz. LEXIS 73; 296 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 22



May 26, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Wagner v. Stewart, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 100087 (D. Ariz., Nov. 8, 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Petition granted by State v. Wagner, 2015 Ariz. App. Unpub. LEXIS 389 (2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Court of Appeals No. 1 CA-CR 97-0092. Maricopa County No. CR 94-92394. Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. The Honorable Barbara M. Jarrett, Judge. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One. 275 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 37, 194 Ariz. 1, 976 P.2d 250 (App. 1998).
State v. Wagner, 194 Ariz. 1, 976 P.2d 250, 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 140 (Ariz. Ct. App., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County AFFIRMED. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One VACATED IN PART; APPROVED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which affirmed his convictions and sentences for first-degree murder and attempted armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder and attempted armed robbery and was sentenced to life imprisonment without parole and seven and one half years, respectively. He sought review and alleged that the murder sentencing statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-703, violated his due process and equal protection rights and that autopsy photographs were improperly admitted. The appellate court affirmed but used a balancing test to find that appellant did not have a due process right to sentencing guidelines for the murder charge. Appellant sought review. The court affirmed in part and vacated in part. The court held that the sentencing statute was not vague, that it did not violate appellant's constitutional rights, and that autopsy photographs were properly admitted because their probative value outweighed the risk of prejudice. However, the appellate court improperly used the balancing test. The statute was not vague because it clearly stated the possible penalties for first-degree murder. The due process balancing test applied to administrative proceedings, not criminal proceedings. Appellant was not constitutionally entitled to sentencing guidelines in a first-degree murder case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions and sentences for first-degree murder and attempted armed robbery, but vacated that part of the appellate court opinion that applied an administrative procedure due process test. The court held that the murder sentencing statute was not vague and did not violate appellant's due process and equal protection rights. The court also found that the autopsy photographs were properly admitted.

 

9 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Aros v. Benefit Arizona Inc.


Supreme Court No. CV-97-0502-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


194 Ariz. 62; 977 P.2d 784; 1999 Ariz. LEXIS 59; 294 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 9



April 20, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Court of Appeals, No. 1 CA-CV 96-0393. Maricopa County, No. C-578634. Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Mark F. Aceto, Judge. Memorandum Decision of the Court of Appeals, Division One, filed October 9, 1997.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court, REVERSED AND REMANDED. Memorandum Decision of the Court of Appeals, VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff consumers appealed a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Arizona), which affirmed dismissal of their class action against defendant lenders alleging violations of the Consumer Loan Act on the grounds that lenders licensed under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 6-602(A) were able to make loans between 1980 and 1984 without being subject to the statute's restrictions.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed a judgment that affirmed dismissal of plaintiff consumers' class action alleging that defendant lenders violated the Consumer Loan Act (CLA) by selling unwanted and unnecessary insurance, making unexplained and unauthorized charges, and establishing payment plans with prohibited balloon payments on the grounds that the version of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 6-602(A), in effect between 1980 and 1984, excepted licensed lenders from the CLA's restrictions. Finding that the language of the statute was ambiguous, the court was required to determine the legislative intent by interpreting the statute as a whole taking into account the statute's context, subject matter, historical background, effects and consequences, and spirit and purpose. The court concluded that the legislative purposes and goals mandated a requirement that licensed consumer lenders submit to the CLA's non-interest restrictions, even though they were allowed to charge any interest agreed to in writing. Any decision otherwise would have nullified the CLA during those years and rendered the legislature's actions futile.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment affirming dismissal of plaintiff consumers' class action against defendant lenders for violations of the Consumer Loan Act (CLA) because the legislative purposes and goals underlying the statute mandated a requirement that licensed consumer lenders submit to the CLA's non-interest restrictions despite their freedom to charge any interest agreed to in writing.

 

10 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Musser


Supreme Court No. CR-97-0367-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


194 Ariz. 31; 977 P.2d 131; 1999 Ariz. LEXIS 36; 292 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 11



March 23, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Court of Appeals No. 1 CA-CR 95-0849. Maricopa County No. LC 95-00536. Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. The Honorable Christopher M. Skelly, Judge. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, 191 Ariz. 228, 954 P.2d 1053 (App. 1998).



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County AFFIRMED. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution appealed the decision of the Court of Appeals, Division One (Arizona), granting appellant standing to challenge Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2916.A and reversing his conviction under § 13-2916.A because it was facially overbroad.


OVERVIEW: Appellant phoned the office of the chief justice of the Arizona Supreme Court to complain. The chief justice was not available, and appellant stated that he might have to show up on the judge's doorstep and discuss the matter at gunpoint. Appellant was convicted of telephone harassment under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2916.A. On review, the appellate court determined appellant had standing and found that § 13-2916.A was unconstitutional because it was facially overbroad. The prosecution sought review, claiming appellant did not have standing to challenge § 13-2916.A. The court vacated and reinstate appellant's conviction, holding that the appellate court erred in granting appellant standing to challenge § 13-2916.A because it did not pose a real and substantial danger to protected expression of parties not before the court, and any misuse of the statute could be addressed and cured through case-by-case analysis of specific facts.


OUTCOME: Grant of standing to challenge telephone harassment statute and reversal of telephone harassment conviction were vacated and conviction was reinstated because appellant did not have standing to challenge the statute in that it did not pose a real and substantial danger to protected expression of parties not before the court.

 

11 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Medina


Supreme Court No. CR-96-0289-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


193 Ariz. 504; 975 P.2d 94; 1999 Ariz. LEXIS 27; 290 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 19



March 4, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Medina, 2013 Ariz. LEXIS 167 (Ariz., Aug. 22, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Maricopa County No. CR 93-08378. Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. The Honorable Brian Hauser, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence for first-degree murder, burglary in the third degree, and aggravated robbery before the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged and convicted of first-degree murder, burglary in the third degree, and aggravated robbery after running over an elderly man while attempting to steal the victim's car and radio. The trial judge sentenced him to aggravated terms of five years for the burglary, seven years for the robbery, and to death for the murder. Defendant appealed the convictions and sentences asserting that the trial judge should have recused himself, that refusal to strike a juror was error, and that the court failed to properly weigh aggravating and mitigating factors in sentencing. The court affirmed the conviction and sentences after finding that the judge was not required to recuse himself, that the juror in question did not demonstrate preconceived notions regarding defendant's guilt, and that the mitigating circumstances were not sufficiently substantial to warrant leniency in light of the aggravating factors present in the case.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences for murder, burglary, and robbery were affirmed because the court properly considered aggravating and mitigating circumstances when imposing sentence and there was no error at trial.

 

12 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


Supreme Court No. CR-97-0389-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


193 Ariz. 452; 974 P.2d 431; 1999 Ariz. LEXIS 16; 290 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



February 23, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended April 12, 1999. Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5926.
Writ of certiorari denied Smith v. Arizona, 528 U.S. 880, 120 S. Ct. 191, 145 L. Ed. 2d 161, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5926 (1999)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Claim dismissed by, Motion denied by Smith v. Schriro, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 11836 (D. Ariz., Mar. 21, 2006)
Subsequent civil proceeding at Dickens v. Brewer, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 57703 (D. Ariz., July 1, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Coconino County No. CR-95-0749. Appeal from the Superior Court of Arizona in Coconino County. The Honorable H. Jeffrey Coker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for first-degree murder, armed robbery, and first-degree burglary from the Coconino County Superior Court (Arizona). Defendant argued that his statements to the police were not voluntary.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of first-degree murder, armed robbery, and first-degree burglary. The trial court sentenced him to death for the murder convictions. After he was picked up by police for questioning, defendant made incriminating statements. Defendant later agreed to talk after his Miranda warnings were given. When a detective told defendant that they had found the bloody weapons and clothes, defendant invoked his right to a lawyer and the interrogation stopped. The court noted that because confessions were presumed involuntary, the state must show by a preponderance of the evidence that a confession was voluntary. The court will look at the totality of the circumstances to determine whether police conduct constituted overreaching. His speech was clear. He was not unkempt. He was not hysterical, hallucinating, or disoriented. On the contrary, he was friendly and cooperative. Defendant appeared to understand his discussions with police, was aware of his rights, and could communicate. No evidence existed that police conduct coerced him to speak. Therefore the judgment was affirmed on appeal because defendant's confession was voluntary.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions for murder, burglary, and armed robbery were affirmed because the court found that the statements given by defendant to the police were voluntary as defendant was not under the influence of drugs or otherwise impaired at the time of his questioning.

 

13 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Kotterman v. Killian


Supreme Court No. CV-97-0412-SA


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


193 Ariz. 273; 972 P.2d 606; 1999 Ariz. LEXIS 8; 288 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 5



January 26, 1999, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 6553.


PRIOR HISTORY: SPECIAL ACTION.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED, RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, various individuals, challenged the constitutionality of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 43-1089, which allowed a state tax credit for those who donated to school tuition organizations, on the grounds that the law violated the Federal Establishment Clause and three provisions of the Arizona Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The court denied petitioners' action for relief, finding that the tuition tax credit provided in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 43-1089 was a neutral adjustment mechanism for equalizing tax burdens and encouraging educational expenditures. Petitioners, various individuals, had challenged the constitutionality of the provision, which allowed a state tax credit of up to 500 dollars for those who donated to school tuition organizations. The court found that petitioners failed to demonstrate that the provision violated either the United States Constitution or the Arizona Constitution. The court found that the tuition tax credit did not prefer one religion over another, or religion over non-religion. It aided a broad spectrum of citizens, allowed a wide range of private choices, and did not have the primary effect of either advancing or inhibiting religion. The court also found no excessive government entanglement with religion as the state did not involve itself in the distribution of funds or in monitoring their application. Any perceived state connection to private religious schools was indirect and attenuated.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioners' action for relief, as it found that the tuition tax credit was a neutral adjustment mechanism for equalizing tax burdens and encouraging educational expenditures. Petitioners failed to demonstrate that it violated either the Federal or the Arizona Constitutions.

 

14 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


San Carlos Apache Tribe v. Superior Court


Supreme Court No. CV-95-0161-SA


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


193 Ariz. 195; 972 P.2d 179; 1999 Ariz. LEXIS 5; 286 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 14



January 23, 1999, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Counsel Amended January 15, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: SPECIAL ACTION. Certification Order filed October 3, 1996. by the Honorable Susan R. Bolton, Judge. Superior Court in Maricopa County.

In Re the General Adjudication of All Rights to Use Water in the Gila River System and Source. Maricopa County No. W-1 (Salt), W-2 (Verde), W-3 (Upper Gila), W-4 (San Pedro) (Consolidated). In Re the General Adjudication of All Rights to Use Water in the Little Colorado River System and Source. Apache County No. 6417.



DISPOSITION: RELIEF GRANTED IN PART AND DENIED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners Indian tribes and the United States challenged the constitutionality of legislative measures that revised many portions of Arizona's surface water law. Respondents, the state land department, several mining entities, and a river project sought to uphold the legislation.


OVERVIEW: A complex litigation evolved around Arizona's surface water law where petitioners Indian tribes and United States challenged the constitutionality of legislative measures that revised the law. Respondents, the state land department, mining entities, and a river project, sought to uphold the legislation. Petitioners asserted that a strict scrutiny standard applied and that the statute impermissibly affected vested substantive rights. Respondents argued there was a presumption that all statutes were constitutional. On review, the court held that the statute impermissibly affected vested substantive rights and that a number of the statutory changes violated the separation of powers clause, Ariz. Const. art. III, because the statute purported to change both substantive and evidentiary law in midstream of a pending case. The court found that the Legislature attempted to control both the legislative and judiciary process and deprived the court of its constitutional authority to find facts and to define and apply the law. The court did uphold certain procedural aspects of the legislation, however, the statute was found unconstitutional where it violated principles of separation of powers.


OUTCOME: The court upheld procedural aspects of the surface water law legislation but the statute was found unconstitutional where a number of the statutory changes violated the Arizona Constitution and principles of separation of powers. The court held that the legislation impermissibly affected vested substantive rights and evidentiary law in midstream of a pending case.

 

15 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Doerr


Supreme Court No. CR-96-0679-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


193 Ariz. 56; 969 P.2d 1168; 1998 Ariz. LEXIS 640; 282 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 14



November 12, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied April 19, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 2693. As Corrected November 13, 1998.
Writ of certiorari denied Doerr v. Arizona, 526 U.S. 1073, 143 L. Ed. 2d 555, 119 S. Ct. 1471, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 2693 (1999)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Doerr v. Schriro, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 22304 (D. Ariz., Sept. 26, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Maricopa County No. CR 94-08531. Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. The Honorable Ronald Reinstein, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment entered on a jury verdict by the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted him of first degree murder, felony murder, sexual assault, and kidnapping, and from the imposition of the death sentence entered upon the trial judge's finding of the heinous, cruel, or depraved aggravator and insufficient mitigation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from the judgment convicting him of first degree murder, felony murder, sexual assault, and kidnapping, and from the imposition of the death sentence. The court affirmed. The jury panel was not tainted by comments of two excused potential jurors. They did not have special knowledge and their comments did not constitute impermissible vouching, as they were neither prosecutors nor witnesses, and defendant's right to cross-examine was not curtailed. The court's excusing teachers from the jury pool was not error, as U.S. Const. amend. VI did not guarantee a specific makeup of a fair and impartial jury. The admission of in life, crime scene, and autopsy photographs was within the discretion of the trial court, and any error would have been harmless, as they did not beyond a reasonable doubt effect the outcome. The court conducted an independent review of the aggravating and mitigating circumstances and found that the heinous, cruel, or depraved aggravator was established by the presence of relishing, mutilation, and gratuitous violence. Defendant did not meet his burden with regard to the mitigating factors as he failed to establish a causal link with the crimes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of first degree murder, felony murder, sexual assault, and kidnapping, and from the imposition of the death sentence. The admission of photographic evidence was within the discretion of the trial court and would have constituted harmless error, the jury pool was not tainted, and defendant failed to meet his burden of proving a causal link of mitigating circumstances to the crimes.

 

16 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Sears v. Hull


Supreme Court No. CV-97-0477-T/AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


192 Ariz. 65; 961 P.2d 1013; 1998 Ariz. LEXIS 75; 273 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 36



July 16, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Court of Appeals No. 1 CA-CV 97-0507. Maricopa County No. CV 97-08942. Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. The Honorable B. Michael Dann, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, governor, State, and Indian tribe, appealed the order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which determined that plaintiff concerned citizens' special action to enjoin the governor from issuing a gaming compact to the Indian tribe, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 5-601.01, raised questions of public importance that entitled the trial court the right to waive the standing requirement.


OVERVIEW: The Indian tribe challenged the order of the trial court, which denied the tribe's motions alleging that the concerned citizens did not have standing to bring their special action to enjoin the governor and the State from issuing a gaming compact to the Indian tribe, pursuant § 5-601.01. The trial court indicated that because the concerned citizens' claims raised questions of public importance, the trial court could waive the strict standing requirements. The court reversed the order of the trial court and held that as a matter of discretion, the court could waive the requirement of standing; however, it would do so only in exceptional circumstances, generally in cases involving issues of great public importance that were likely to recur. The concerned citizens' action did not present issues of such great public importance that would have influenced the court to waive standing. The case did not raise fundamental questions of statutory construction or of the constitutionality of a statute or government action. Therefore, standing could not have been waived.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the order of the trial court.

 

17 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Hull v. Albrecht


Supreme Court No. CV-98-0238-SA


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


192 Ariz. 34; 960 P.2d 634; 1998 Ariz. LEXIS 59; 271 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 7



June 16, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED IN PART; ORDER MODIFIED. As Corrected June 17, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Maricopa County No. CV 91-13087. Special Action from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. The Honorable Rebecca A. Albrecht, Judge.
Roosevelt Elementary Sch. Dist. No. 66 v. Bishop, 179 Ariz. 233, 877 P.2d 806, 1994 Ariz. LEXIS 79 (Ariz., 1994)



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED IN PART; ORDER MODIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner governor sought review of legislation designed to provide a general and uniform public school system in Arizona by special action from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner governor filed a request for special action against respondents, state officials and school boards, seeking a declaration that new legislation attempting to create a school financing system was constitutional under the mandate of Ariz. Const. art. XI, § 1 to provide a general and uniform public school system. The court found that through the legislation, the state created the required minimum adequacy standards for capital facilities and ensured, through state funding, that all districts complied with these standards. However, the court determined that the legislation failed to fulfill the requirement that the state fund public schools through a financing system that did not cause substantial disparities between the districts. The funding mechanism of the legislation caused substantial disparities between opt-out and participating districts, thereby formalizing and perpetuating a structure that failed the general and uniform test. The court refused to sever the unconstitutional portion of the legislation and give effect to the statute's constitutional portions in deference to legislative authority and intent; thus, it invalidated the entire legislation.


OUTCOME: The court invalidated legislation designed to provide a general and uniform public school system in Arizona because the statute failed to fulfill the constitutional requirement that the state fund public schools through a financing system that did not cause substantial disparities between the districts.

 

18 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


O'Day v. McDonnell Douglas Helicopter Co.


Supreme Court No. CV-97-0274-CQ


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


191 Ariz. 535; 959 P.2d 792; 1998 Ariz. LEXIS 52; 270 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 23; 13 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1868



May 26, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] United States District Court. No. CV-91-777-PGR. Certified Questions from the United States District Court for the District of Arizona. The Honorable Paul G. Rosenblatt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: QUESTIONS ANSWERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States District Court for the District of Arizona certified questions to the court in plaintiff former employee's age discrimination action against defendant former employer. The questions concerned whether the after-acquired evidence defense applied to a case of wrongful discharge or a case of breach of employment contract, and if it applied, how the defense limited or precluded recovery of damages.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff former employee brought an age discrimination action after defendant former employer failed to promote him and laid him off. After discovery began, defendant learned that plaintiff had searched his supervisor's office and copied documents useful to his claim. The district court granted summary judgment for defendant on the after-acquired evidence defense. After the appellate court reversed the dismissal, the district court certified questions to the court. The court held that after-acquired evidence of employee misconduct was no defense to a tortious wrongful termination action, but it was relevant to remedies. If an employer demonstrated that it would have fired an employee had it known of prior misconduct, reinstatement and front pay would not be available but lost earnings would be available. However, after-acquired evidence did not bar other compensatory damages due to the employer's wrongful conduct. The court also held that after-acquired evidence of employee misconduct was a defense to a breach of contract action for wages and benefits lost as a result of discharge if the employer demonstrated that it would have fired the employee had it known of the misconduct.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified questions. After-acquired evidence of employee misconduct was no defense to a wrongful termination action. However, it was relevant to remedies if the employer would have fired the employee had it known of prior misconduct. The evidence was a defense to a breach of contract action for wages and benefits lost as a result of discharge if the employer would have fired the employee had it known of prior misconduct.

 

19 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Ruiz v. Hull


Supreme Court No. CV-96-0493-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


191 Ariz. 441; 957 P.2d 984; 1998 Ariz. LEXIS 34; 268 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



April 28, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied January 11, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 490.


PRIOR HISTORY: Court of Appeals No. 1 CA-CV 94-0235. Maricopa County No. CV 92-19603. Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. The Honorable Jeffrey S. Cates, Judge. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division,     Ariz.   ,     P.2d     (App. 1996).



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County REVERSED WITH DIRECTIONS. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, governor, attorney general, and sponsors sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals of Maricopa County (Arizona), which reversed in part and affirmed in part a trial court decision and held that Ariz. Const. art. XXVIII was unconstitutional in favor of plaintiffs, employees and officials.


OVERVIEW: The sponsors initiated a petition drive to amend Arizona's constitution to designate English as the state's official language and to require state and local governments to conduct business in English only. After the initiative was successful, the state employees and officials brought an action challenging the constitutionality of Ariz. Const. art. XXVIII. The trial court declared the article constitutional, but the lower court reversed that decision. The court reversed the trial court's decision and vacated the lower court's opinion. The court rejected the attorney general's narrow construction of the article because the attorney general's opinion did not comport with the article's plain meaning or with the drafter's intent. Further, the article violated the First Amendment by depriving public officials and employees of the ability to communicate with the public. The court held that the article violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment because it unduly burdened the core right of non-English speaking individuals to petition the government for redress. The goal to promote English as a common language did not require a total prohibition on non-English usage.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and vacated the lower court's opinion, holding that the article was unconstitutional in favor of the employees and officials.

 

20 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Trostle


Supreme Court No. CR-94-0175-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


191 Ariz. 4; 951 P.2d 869; 1997 Ariz. LEXIS 145; 259 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 13



December 24, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County. The Honorable Richard Nichols, Judge. Pima County No. CR-43195.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; SENTENCE REDUCED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of first degree murder, armed robbery, kidnapping, and theft by control. The Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) sentenced defendant to death for the murder and to consecutive and concurrent prison terms for the other offenses. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found two aggravating factors: (1) that there was an expectation of pecuniary gain, and (2) that the killing was especially heinous, cruel, or depraved. It determined that the mitigation evidence was insufficient to call for leniency. The court affirmed the defendant's non-capital sentences, but reduced his death sentence. It held that defendant presented substantial mitigation evidence. Defendant established, by a preponderance of the evidence, that he was affected by an impaired ability to conform his conduct to the law's requirements. The trial court's denial of defendant's motion for change of venue was within its discretion. The trial court did not err when it denied defendant's request to excuse venirepersons. The facts established beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was a major participant in the murder and acted with reckless indifference to human life.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and non-capital sentences were affirmed. His sentence of death was reduced to natural life imprisonment without possibility of release, to be served consecutively to the prison terms for the non-capital convictions.

Hull v. Albrecht


Supreme Court No. CV-97-0369-SA


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


190 Ariz. 520; 950 P.2d 1141; 1997 Ariz. LEXIS 135; 259 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 5



December 23, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by Hull v. Albrecht, 1998 Ariz. LEXIS 353 (Ariz., Feb. 18, 1998)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Maricopa County No. CV 91-13087. Special Action from the Superior Court of Arizona in Maricopa County. The Honorable Rebecca A. Albrecht, Judge.
Roosevelt Elementary Sch. Dist. No. 66 v. Bishop, 179 Ariz. 233, 877 P.2d 806, 1994 Ariz. LEXIS 79 (Ariz., 1994)



DISPOSITION: APPROVED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner governor of Arizona sought review of the order of the Superior Court of Arizona in Maricopa County, which denied the governor's motion for a declaration that amendments to the state's school finance legislation complied with the court's mandate.


OVERVIEW: The legislature amended the school financing system to include the Assistance to Build Classrooms (ABC) fund, which attempted to remedy disparity among the districts by providing need-based income to poor districts to be used as expenditures, saved, or as the basis for issuing bonds. The court found that the ABC legislation did not address the core problem of heavy reliance upon property taxation, and that it imposed different tax burdens on citizens in different districts to support the state's obligation to provide for the education of its students pursuant to Ariz. Const. art. XI, § 1. The court noted that the voters could allow a district to opt out of the system by not issuing bonds, and that the amount granted was not related to actual need of the districts. The legislation gave districts the power to choose substandard facilities, which was not what the court had mandated. The court held that the legislation did not meet the constitutional requirements for funding education.


OUTCOME: The court approved the superior court's denial of the governor's motion for a declaration that amendments to the state's school finance legislation were in compliance with the court's mandate.

State v. Schackart


Supreme Court No. CR-93-0535-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


190 Ariz. 238; 947 P.2d 315; 1997 Ariz. LEXIS 125; 255 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



October 30, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Schackart v. Arizona, 525 U.S. 862, 119 S. Ct. 149, 142 L. Ed. 2d 122, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 5503 (1998)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Claim dismissed by, Motion denied by Schackart v. Schriro, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 86821 (D. Ariz., Nov. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Pima County. No. Cr-12818. Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County. The Honorable Michael Brown, Judge.
State v. Schackart, 175 Ariz. 494, 858 P.2d 639, 1993 Ariz. LEXIS 59 (Ariz., 1993)



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which sentenced defendant to death for aggravated assault.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of first degree murder, kidnapping, and sexual assault. The trial court sentenced him to death for the homicide and to consecutive thirty-year prison terms on the other charges. This court affirmed the convictions and non-capital sentences on direct appeal. Deficiencies in the record, however, required the court to vacate the death sentence and remand for resentencing. Thereafter, the trial court found two statutory aggravators, A.R.S. § 13-703(F)(2) (prior violent felony) and (F)(6) (especially cruel, heinous, or depraved murder). The trial court resentenced defendant to death, and this automatic appeal followed. Concerned that the (F)(2) factor might be overturned on appeal, the State filed a "Request to Take Judicial Notice," and asserted that in order for this court to intelligently resolve the dispute, it must have proof before it of the materials demonstrating the precise nature of the prior convictions. The court held that there was nothing in the record to indicate that the sentencing judge overstepped boundaries. The court found that having reweighed the evidence, mitigation was not sufficiently substantial to call for leniency.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the sentence.

 

23 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Spreitz


Supreme Court No. CR-94-0454-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


190 Ariz. 129; 945 P.2d 1260; 1997 Ariz. LEXIS 103; 252 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



September 11, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Pima County Superior Court No. CR-27745. Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County. The Honorable William N. Sherrill, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pima County Superior Court (Arizona) convicted defendant of first degree murder, sexual assault, and kidnapping. Defendant was sentenced to death for the murder and to 14-year consecutive prison terms for each of the non-capital convictions. Appeal to the court for the death sentence was mandatory.


OVERVIEW: The court on appeal affirmed defendant's convictions and death sentence. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in not granting his motion to dismiss for violation of his right to a speedy trial. The court held that defendant repeatedly and knowingly waived his Ariz. R. Crim. P. 8 speedy trial rights by filing a signed acknowledgment that recognized the requested continuances would move his trial outside the Ariz. R. Crim. P. 8.2 limits. The court held that defendant did not file a motion to dismiss for violation of his speedy trial rights until after the evidentiary hearings were terminated and after trial had been set. The court found that although the period between defendant's arraignment and trial was unprecedented, defendant waived his right to object by not objecting when the violation was occurring. The court held that admission of photographs of the victim was harmless because based on the overwhelming evidence against defendant, the jury would have found him guilty without the photographs. The court found that the aggravating circumstance of especial cruelty in defendant's murder of the victim outweighed all factors mitigating in favor of leniency.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence. The court held that defendant's right to a speedy trial was not violated. The court held that the aggravating circumstance of the crime outweighed all mitigating factors of leniency.

State v. Lee


Supreme Court No. CR-94-0237-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


189 Ariz. 590; 944 P.2d 1204; 1997 Ariz. LEXIS 97; 250 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 24



August 26, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Lee v. Arizona, 523 U.S. 1007, 118 S. Ct. 1192, 140 L. Ed. 2d 321, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 1687 (1998)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Stay dissolved by, Certificate of appealability granted, in part Lee v. Schriro, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 324 (D. Ariz., Jan. 6, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Maricopa County Superior Court No. CR 92-04225. Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. The Honorable Ronald S. Reinstein, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction and sentences in the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona), of kidnapping, sexual assault, armed robbery, theft, and two counts of first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, along with another, killed and robbed two victims. Defendant was convicted of kidnapping, sexual assault, armed robbery, theft, and two counts of first degree murder. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentences. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that pursuant to Ariz. R. Evid. 13.3(a)(3), if the trial court properly found the offenses were alleged to have been part of a common scheme or plan, defendant was not entitled to severance as of right. In addition, the court held there was substantial evidence that reasonable persons accepted as adequate and sufficient to support a conclusion of defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that proceedings were open to the public, including the news media, unless the court found, upon application of defendant, that an open proceeding presented a clear and present danger to defendant's right to a fair trial by an impartial jury. In addition, the court held that the trial court must have considered all evidence offered in mitigation but was not bound to accept all such evidence as mitigating.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentences of defendant.

 

25 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lee


Supreme Court No. CR-94-0367-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


189 Ariz. 608; 944 P.2d 1222; 1997 Ariz. LEXIS 98; 250 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 34



August 26, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Lee v. Arizona, 523 U.S. 1007, 118 S. Ct. 1192, 140 L. Ed. 2d 321, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 1687 (1998)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Stay dissolved by, Certificate of appealability granted, in part Lee v. Schriro, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 324 (D. Ariz., Jan. 6, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Maricopa County Superior Court No. CR 92-04225. Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. The Honorable Ronald S. Reinstein, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona) convicted defendant of first degree murder and armed robbery. He was sentenced to death for the murder conviction and to a term in prison for the armed robbery. He had an automatic appeal of the convictions and the sentences.


OVERVIEW: The defendant confessed to robbing a market and shooting the clerk. Prior to his conviction for the murder and armed robbery, he was convicted for two other murders that he committed after the robbery and murder. On appeal, he challenged the findings of aggravation and mitigation related to his sentences. The court held that it independently determined whether the aggravating circumstances was proven beyond a reasonable doubt, considered any mitigating circumstances, and then weighed the circumstances to decide whether the mitigating circumstances were sufficiently substantial to call for leniency. The convictions for the two murders could be considered during his sentencing hearing regardless of the order in which the underlying crimes were committed. The sentencing court was required to consider the prior conviction because it involved the use of violence on another person. Also, the fact that the murder was both senseless and gratuitous supported a finding of aggravating circumstances. Though the defendant proved age, lack of significant prior criminal history, and deprived childhood, those mitigating circumstances did not achieve the qualitative level requisite for leniency.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions for first degree murder and armed robbery and the sentences imposed for each.

 

26 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Getz


Supreme Court No. CR-96-0595-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


189 Ariz. 561; 944 P.2d 503; 1997 Ariz. LEXIS 93; 250 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 10



August 14, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 25, 1997.
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Allison, 2004 Ariz. App. Unpub. LEXIS 347 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Court of Appeals No. 2 CA-CR 94-0184, 2 CA-CR 95-0543-PR (Consolidated). Pima County No. CR-43000. Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County. The Honorable Leslie Miller, Judge. Memorandum Decision of the Court of Appeals, Division Two, Filed July 30, 1996.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County AFFIRMED IN PART REVERSED IN PART. Memorandum Decision of the Court of Appeals, Division Two, APPROVED IN PART VACATED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Court of Appeals (Arizona), affirming his conviction for sexual abuse under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1404(A). He asserted that the trial court erred in ruling that the state did not have to prove lack of consent in a prosecution for sexual abuse where the victim was 16 years of age.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sexual abuse of a 16 year old pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1404(A) and was sentenced. The appellate court affirmed and he sought review, asserting that the trial court erred in denying his request for directed verdict of acquittal and in ruling that the state did not have to prove lack of consent. The court reversed. Concerned about the constitutional ramifications of reading the affirmative defense statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1407, into the definitional statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1404, it applied § 13-1404 as written. It held that § 13-1404 was clear and that persons of ordinary intelligence reading it would conclude that, if the victim was 14 or over, the state must prove lack of consent. Reading both § 13-1404 (sexual abuse) and § 13-1401 (definition of consent), it ruled that one would clearly be led to believe that a person between the ages of 14 and 17 could consent for purposes of § 13-1404. The state acknowledged that the undisputed evidence showed that the victim/participant consented to the touching of her breasts. Therefore, the court held that the trial court should have granted judgments of acquittal on relevant counts.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the decision of the court of appeals to the extent that it held that the state did not have to prove lack of consent. The uncontested evidence established that the victim had consented to the touching of her breasts and judgment of acquittal on the sexual abuse counts should have been granted. The conviction on other related counts was affirmed.

 

27 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Woods v. Block


Supreme Court No. CV-96-0461-SA


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


189 Ariz. 269; 942 P.2d 428; 1997 Ariz. LEXIS 78; 247 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 22



July 15, 1997, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JURISDICTION ACCEPTED. RELIEF GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorney general for the state of Arizona filed a petition for special action against respondent members of the Arizona Constitutional Defense Council (CDC) that requested that the court find Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-401 (1996) was unconstitutional and that the CDC was prohibited from exercising its purported powers and expending public funds.


OVERVIEW: Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-401 (1994) created CDC to advance Arizona's sovereignty over state issues. Actions on its behalf were brought by the attorney general or outside legal counsel. But only the attorney general could negotiate contracts with outside counsel and approve claims for legal fees. Section 41-401 was amended in 1996 to remove the veto power of the attorney general and his power over the funds. The court held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-401 (1996) was unconstitutional and that (1) the court had jurisdiction over the action under Ariz. Const. art. VI, § 5.1; (2) the attorney general had standing under Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 35-212, 12-2041 because his challenge to the constitutionality of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-401 (1996) was in support of his authority to prevent the improper expenditure of public funds and the relief requested was under his quo warranto authority; (3) the attorney general's request to prohibit the CDC from exercising its power to litigate included a request to prohibit payment for such litigation; and (4) § 41-401, as amended, violated Ariz. Const. art. III because CDC was a legislative body that was performing an executive function.


OUTCOME: The court granted relief to an attorney general and held that the statute was unconstitutional and that the CDC had no authority to act thereunder.

 

28 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Riggs


Supreme Court No. CR-96-0351-PR, Supreme Court No. CR-96-0342-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


189 Ariz. 327; 942 P.2d 1159; 1997 Ariz. LEXIS 79; 247 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 7



July 15, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Court of Appeals No. 1 CA-CR 94-0970. Maricopa County No. CR-93-93493. Court of Appeals No. 1 CA-CR 94-0926. Maricopa County No. CR 94-90907. State v. Riggs. Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. The Honorable Daniel A. Barker, Judge. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One VACATED. State v. Taggart. Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. The Honorable Christopher M. Skelly, Judge. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, 186 Ariz. 569 925 P.2d 710 (App. 1996).



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County AFFIRMED. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted in separate trials on unrelated offenses. As to one defendant, the Court of Appeals (Arizona) held that a defendant was always permitted to bring out at trial a victim's refusal of a pretrial interview with the defendant, and as to the other defendant, held that a defendant never permitted to bring out at trial a victim's refusal of a pretrial interview with the defendant.


OVERVIEW: The court consolidated cases on review, the state contended that the Victim's Bill of Rights implicitly provided victims a constitutional right not to be cross-examined on their refusal to grant a pretrial interview. The court determined that the right to refuse a pretrial interview was not analogous to a defendant's right to remain silent because the rights derived from two different purposes. The court held that asking the victim at trial about his or her refusal to grant a pretrial interview did not result in any greater breach of the victim's privacy, or greater contact with the defendant, than is already necessary. Defendants contended that the trial courts' decisions to restrict the cross-examination of the victims violated their federal and state constitutional rights to confront and cross-examine the witnesses against them. The court held that because defendants failed to make a showing that the victims refused the interviews for a reason bearing on their credibility, the trial court's limitations on defendant's cross-examination did not violate defendant's constitutional rights to confront adverse witnesses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions and vacated the opinions of the court of appeals.

 

29 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Mazen v. Seidel


Supreme Court No. CV-96-0379-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


189 Ariz. 195; 940 P.2d 923; 1997 Ariz. LEXIS 62; 245 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 29



June 10, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Court of Appeals No. 1 CA-SA 95-0355. Maricopa County No. CR 95-05456. Special Action from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Honorable John H. Seidel, Judge. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One,    Ariz.    ,     P.2d    , 1996 Ariz. App. LEXIS 104 (1996).



DISPOSITION: Special Action from the Superior Court in Maricopa County ORDER APPROVED. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent trial judge and real party in interest state appealed from a decision of the Court of Appeals, Division One (Arizona), which found in favor of petitioner defendant and ruled that the trial judge should have suppressed evidence seized by the police after a fire in a rented storage unit.


OVERVIEW: Firefighters responded to a fire at a storage unit rented by defendant. While extinguishing the fire, one firefighter called the police after he saw plants that appeared to be marijuana. The police arrived during the clean-up operation, observed the plants, and then seized the plants, growing equipment, and several garbage bags filled with marijuana. After being arrested and criminally charged, defendant filed a motion to suppress the evidence. The trial judge denied the motion, but the appellate court vacated the trial judge's order. On appeal, the court reversed, concluding that the seizure did not violate U.S. Const. amend. IV or Ariz. Const. art. II, § 8. Specifically, the court held that the firefighters' warrantless entry into the storage unit had been proper under the exigent circumstances. Moreover, the court ruled that because the police officers responded to the firefighter's call and entered the storage unit while the firefighters were still on the scene and because the police officers confined themselves to the area in which the firefighters were working and made no additional inspection, the seizure of contraband in plain view was permissible.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's ruling and affirmed the trial judge's denial of defendant's motion to suppress. In particular, the court held that because the police officers responded to the firefighter's call and because the police officers confined their search to the area in which the firefighters were working, the seizure of contraband in plain view was permissible.

 

30 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


R.L. Augustine Constr. Co. v. Peoria Unified Sch. Dist. No. 11


Supreme Court No. CV-95-0299-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


188 Ariz. 368; 936 P.2d 554; 1997 Ariz. LEXIS 48; 241 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 17



April 22, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified May 21, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Court of Appeals No. 1 CA-CV 93-0107. Maricopa County No. CV 91-17068. Appeal from the Superior Court of Arizona in Maricopa County. The Honorable William P. Sargeant, III, Judge. Opinion of the Court of Appeals Division One. 183 Ariz. 393, 904 P.2d 462 (App. 1995).



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court of Arizona in Maricopa County REVERSED AND REMANDED. Opinion of the Court of Appeals Division One VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant school district governing board petitioned for review of an opinion of the Arizona Court of Appeals, which held that the governing board's procurement rules were unconstitutional and that the Administrative Review Act did not apply to school districts and reversed the superior court's judgment, which dismissed plaintiff contractor's breach of contract claims for failure to seek an administrative rehearing.


OVERVIEW: The governing board entered into a contract with the contractor to build an administration center. A dispute arose, which led to administrative review and a determination by a hearing officer appointed by the governing board. The contractor filed an action for judicial review under the Administrative Review Act and a declaration that the procurement rules were unconstitutional. The superior court dismissed the complaint because the contractor failed to seek an administrative rehearing. The court of appeals held that the procurement rules were unconstitutional and that the Administrative Review Act did not apply to school districts and reversed. The court vacated the opinion of the court of appeals, reversed the superior court's judgment, and remanded for a new trial. The court did not reach the question of constitutionality and held instead that the procurement rules were inconsistent with the State Procurement Code because there was no difference between first- and second-tier administrative review and the rules did not provide a mechanism for judicial review.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the opinion of the court of appeals, reversed the superior court's judgment dismissing the contractor's complaint, and remanded to the superior court for a trial de novo on the respective claims of the contractor and the governing board.

STATE v. MANN


Supreme Court No. CR-95-0077-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


188 Ariz. 220; 934 P.2d 784; 1997 Ariz. LEXIS 26; 238 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 18



March 11, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Mann v. Arizona, 522 U.S. 895, 118 S. Ct. 238, 139 L. Ed. 2d 169, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 5834 (1997)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Towery, 204 Ariz. 386, 64 P.3d 828, 2003 Ariz. LEXIS 16 (Ariz., 2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Stay vacated by, Certificate of appealability granted Mann v. Ryan, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 76290 (D. Ariz., Aug. 10, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Pima County No. CR-44903. Appeal from the Superior Court in Pima County. The Honorable John F. Kelly, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment from the Superior Court in Pima County (Arizona), which convicted him of first degree murder and sentenced him to death. The superior court found aggravating circumstances pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-703(E).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the superior court committed error in admitting inculpatory evidence without determining whether the waiver of defendant's Fifth Amendment rights was knowing, intelligent, and voluntary. The court affirmed the judgment and did not believe a stipulation to facts the state could easily have proved amounted to an exceptional circumstance. Defendant was eligible for the death penalty when the state had proven beyond a reasonable doubt the existence of at least one statutory aggravating circumstance. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-703(E). The court found that the evidence was sufficient to find the murder was cruel because a victim was alive and conscious for an appreciable period of time. Murdering a person to facilitate a robbery and escape constituted murdering for pecuniary gain. No double punishment problem existed because cruelty and multiple homicide were not elements of first degree murder. The court held that disparity in sentences was mitigating only when it was unexplained. The court found that an abusive factor did not affect defendant's behavior at the time of the crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of first degree murder and sentenced him to death. The court found aggravating circumstances and held that disparity in sentencing of an accomplice was not mitigating because it could be explained.

State v. Mott


Supreme Court No. CR-95-0274-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


187 Ariz. 536; 931 P.2d 1046; 1997 Ariz. LEXIS 4; 234 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 7



January 16, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 22, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Court of Appeals No. 2 CA-CR 92-0107. Pima County No. CR-33085. Appeal form the Superior Court in Pima County. The Honorable James C. Carruth, Judge. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division Two, 183 Ariz. 191, 901 P.2d 1221 (App. 1995).



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Pima County AFFIRMED. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division Two, VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with two counts of child abuse and first degree murder, and was convicted. The Court of Appeals, Division Two (Arizona), held that expert psychological testimony that as a battered woman, defendant was unable to form the requisite mental state necessary for the commission of the charged offenses was admissible. Defendant and the state challenged the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the expert psychological testimony was necessary to demonstrate that defendant was not capable of forming the requisite mental state of knowledge or intent, and precluding a defendant from introducing psychological testimony to challenge the mens rea element of a crime violated due process. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred when it admitted certain Ariz. R. Evid. 404(b), evidence. The court found that the Arizona legislature had not provided for a diminished capacity defense, but instead had provided the M'Naghten test as the sole standard for criminal responsibility. Consequently, Arizona did not allow evidence of a defendant's mental disorder short of insanity either as an affirmative defense or to negate the mens rea element of a crime. The court also found that evidence that defendant struck her child and had stated that she wished the child was dead was admissible under Ariz. R. Evid. 404(b), because the probative value of these acts was not substantially outweighed by the danger of unfair prejudice.


OUTCOME: The lower court's judgment was vacated and defendant's conviction was affirmed.

State v. Thornton


Supreme Court No. CR-95-0044-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


187 Ariz. 325; 929 P.2d 676; 1996 Ariz. LEXIS 127; 232 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



December 12, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied May 12, 1996, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 2961.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Cochise County Nos. CR 91-00296 and CR 93-10-00403 [Consolidated]. Appeal from the Superior Court of Arizona in Cochise County. The Honorable James L. Riley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Arizona in Cochise County (Arizona), which found him guilty of first degree murder, burglary, controlling property of another, kidnapping and escape from a correctional facility. The trial court sentenced him to death for murder and to prison for the remaining convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that a juror who listened to his flight and capture on a scanner set should have been excused for cause. The court found, however, that because the facts heard by the juror were not the subject of dispute, she was not a witness in the action. Because the trial judge properly found that she could be fair and impartial, there was no error in not excusing her for cause. Defendant also argued that the trial court's order requiring him to disclose mental health experts and hospitalization records violated his right against self-incrimination. The court held that the order was not testimonial and did not compel him to incriminate himself, therefore there was no self-incrimination issue. Defendant argued that the court erred in not finding mental illness and his character to be mitigating factors. The court found that defendant failed to prove by a preponderance of the evidence that he was unable to either appreciate the wrongfulness of his conduct or to conform his conduct to the requirements of the law. Because defendant's life showed a consistent disregard for the rights of others, the court also held that defendant's character was not a mitigating factor.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed.

State v. Soto-Fong


Supreme Court No. CR-94-0046-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


187 Ariz. 186; 928 P.2d 610; 1996 Ariz. LEXIS 119; 230 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 7



November 19, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 13, 1997. Certiorari Denied May 19, 1997.
