Estate of Hernandez by Hernandez-Wheeler v. Arizona Bd. of Regents


Supreme Court No. CV-92-0079-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


177 Ariz. 244; 866 P.2d 1330; 1994 Ariz. LEXIS 6; 156 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 43



January 13, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Court of Appeals Nos. 2 CA-CV 90-0191, 2 CA-CV 90-0219, 2 CA-CV 90-0252, 2 CA-CV 90-0257. Pima County No. 255362. Appeal from the Superior Court in Pima County. The Honorable Lina S. Rodriguez, Judge. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division Two. 172 Ariz. 522, 838 P.2d 1283 (Ct. App. 1991). Vacated



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff drunk driver victim appealed decision of the Court of Appeals (Arizona) affirming summary judgment for defendants, a college fraternity, its members, and associated entities, holding that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 4-312(B) immunized a non-licensee for liability for serving liquor to a minor who injured a third party.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, a college fraternity, its members, and associated entities, served liquor to a minor and he collided with plaintiff drunk driver victim and paralyzed him. After plaintiff filed suit, defendants moved for summary judgment under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 4-312(B), which provided immunity for a non-licensee. The trial court granted the motion and the court of appeals affirmed. Defendants contended the statute, read with related sections, conferred blanket immunity except for licensees serving minor drinkers or those obviously intoxicated; or, that the statute repealed by implication Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 4-301, which provided for non-licensee immunity. The court held that there was no immunity for non-licensees who served liquor to minors and that this was consistent with the wording of the statutes, the legislative intent, and scheme. Furthermore, the common law of Arizona provided for liability for serving liquor to a minor. The judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court opinion was vacated and the judgment of the trial court was reversed. The case was remanded for further proceedings because there was no statutory or common law immunity for serving liquor to a minor.

Petolicchio v. Santa Cruz County Fair & Rodeo Ass'n


Supreme Court No. CV-92-0198-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


177 Ariz. 256; 866 P.2d 1342; 1994 Ariz. LEXIS 7; 156 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 51



January 13, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Court of Appeals No. 2 CA-CV 91-0220. Santa Cruz County No. 91-V-063. Appeal from the Superior Court of Santa Cruz County. The Honorable Roberto C. Montiel, Judge. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division Two, 172 Ariz. 587, 838 P.2d 1348 (1992), VACATED



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The case was before the court to review the Court of Appeals (Arizona) order, reversing an order dismissing plaintiff decedent's parents' wrongful death action against defendants, liquor licensees and related parties, and declaring Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 4-312(B) unconstitutional to the extent that it granted immunity to defendants.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff decedent's parents filed an action for wrongful death against defendants, liquor licensee and related parties, seeking to recover damages for their son's death in an alcohol-related automobile accident. They alleged that defendant related parties negligently failed to supervise their own son and permitted him to steal liquor. The appellate court vacated the trial court's dismissal of the complaint based on the immunity granted liquor licensees under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 4-312(B) and declared the statute unconstitutional. The court granted review on the statute's constitutionality, but vacated on other grounds, ruling that Arizona's social host and dram shop legislation did not apply. It declared that the case was a matter of common law negligence. It found that defendant liquor licensee, which had notice that minors had access to and were stealing its alcohol, had a duty to take reasonable precautions for the safety of the general public. The theft of the alcohol was not an intervening cause that broke the chain of proximate causation because the subsequent chain of events leading to the accident was foreseeable.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the dismissal of the complaint and the appellate order declaring a dram shop immunity law unconstitutional in plaintiff decedent's parents' wrongful death action against defendants, liquor licensee and related parties. As a matter of common law negligence, defendant liquor licensee owed the general public a duty of to prevent minors from stealing its alcohol. The theft of the liquor did not break the causation chain.

State v. Apelt


No. CR-90-0246-AP/PC


Supreme Court of Arizona

November 9, 1993

Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by State v. Arellano, 213 Ariz. 474, 143 P.3d 1015, 2006 Ariz. LEXIS 61 (Ariz., 2006)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, in part Apelt v. Schriro, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 50526 (D. Ariz., June 16, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Arizona in Pinal County. The Honorable Robert R. Bean, Judge. Pinal County No. CR-14946



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED

OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and conspiracy to commit first degree murder in the death of his wife, and was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed, arguing, inter alia, that he was deprived of a fair trial because jurors saw him in shackles and handcuffs outside the courthouse, the trial court erred in admitting various items that were illegally seized, the trial court erred in denying his request for an ex parte hearing so he could request expert assistance, and the trial court erred in denying his petition for post-conviction relief based on newly discovered evidence. The police were authorized to seize items not listed on the search warrant because they were in plain sight, the court held that the state was not required to equalize the resources of the indigent and the wealthy, and the testimony would not have changed the outcome of the trial because the evidence was overwhelming that defendant forcibly took his wife to the desert with the intent to kill her or assist in killing her.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence because the state was not required to equalize the resources of indigent and wealthy defendants in expert assistance, and the new evidence would not have changed the outcome of defendant's trial because there was overwhelming evidence of his guilt. The court also held that the brief exposure of defendant handcuffed and shackled to jury outside the courtroom was not inherently prejudicial.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Pima County No. CR-21715. Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County. The Honorable Thomas Meehan, Judge
People v. West, 209 Ill. App. 3d 1019, 568 N.E.2d 945, 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 336, 154 Ill. Dec. 724 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., 1991)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction and death sentence in the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) for first-degree felony murder. Defendant argued that the state failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that the killing of the victim was especially cruel and heinous, and that the state failed to find beyond a reasonable doubt that that defendant killed with the expectation of pecuniary gain.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree felony murder and sentenced to death. Defendant sought review of the conviction and the sentence, arguing that the state failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that the killing of the victim was especially cruel or heinous, that the application of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-703(F)(5), expectation of pecuniary gain as an aggravating circumstance, to his case was unconstitutional, that the state failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant killed in expectation of pecuniary gain, and that imposing the death penalty for felony murder was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the conviction and the death sentence, holding that the killing of the victim was heinous because defendant enjoyed the murder, he inflicted unnecessary gratuitous violence to commit the crime, the victim was helpless, and the murder was senseless because it was unnecessary to achieve defendant's goal. The expectation of pecuniary gain was among the causes of the victim's death, and thus the aggravating factor of pecuniary gain was established. The death penalty was appropriate for felony murder, because defendant was a major participant in the burglary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for felony murder and his death sentence, holding that defendant's murder of the victim was heinous because he relished the murder, he inflicted gratuitous violence beyond that necessary to commit the crime, the victim was helpless, and the murder was senseless. The aggravating factor of pecuniary gain was present.

Gotland v. Town of Cave Creek


No. CV-92-0038-PR


Supreme Court of Arizona


175 Ariz. 614; 858 P.2d 1217; 1993 Ariz. LEXIS 77; 147 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 22



September 2, 1993 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Granted September 25, 1992. As Corrected November 30, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Court of Appeals No. 1 CA-CV 89-562. Maricopa County No. CV 88-22657. Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. The Honorable Daniel E. Nastro, Judge. The Honorable Paul A. Katz, Judge. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, 172 Ariz. 397, 837 P.2d 1132 (App. 1991). Vacated



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners sought review of the judgment of the Arizona Court of Appeals, which held, on appeal, that Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 28-1861(B) was constitutional, in an inverse condemnation action brought by the landowners against defendant town, where the trial court had ruled that such statute effected an unconstitutional taking without just compensation.


OVERVIEW: The landowners purchased certain real property, which had a road running across it. The town passed a resolution declaring the road a public roadway pursuant to § 28-1861(B). The landowners filed suit in inverse condemnation and for summary judgment declaring § 28-1861(B) to be unconstitutional. The trial court, ruling that the statute effected an unconstitutional taking without just compensation, granted the landowner's motion. Thereafter, the town sought an injunction against the landowners, but such injunction was denied. The town appealed, and the court of appeals held that § 28-1861(B) was constitutional. The court then granted the landowners' petition for review to determine whether § 28-1861(B) was a curative statute or whether § 28-1861(B) transferred to the state title to land that was used for roadways for specified periods beginning before January 1, 1960. On ruling, the court held that the statute was constitutional and that it was curative. The court held that the statute did not overrule the Arizona common law prohibition against the creation of public highways by prescription. Thus, the court vacated the court of appeals' decision and remanded to the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court held that the statute at issue was curative. Therefore, the court vacated the court of appeals' decision and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

State ex rel. Miller v. Dawson


No. CV-92-0413-SA


Supreme Court of Arizona


175 Ariz. 610; 858 P.2d 1213; 1993 Ariz. LEXIS 80; 147 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 23



September 2, 1993 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Mandate Issued September 23, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Gila County Nos. CV 89-275 and CV 26,142 [Consolidated]



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED, RELIEF DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent property owners filed a complaint in inverse condemnation. The Gila County Superior Court (Arizona) granted partial summary judgment to the property owners. The state then filed an eminent domain action against the property, which was consolidated with the inverse condemnation action. A special action was filed by the state after the trial court refused to reconsider its partial summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The property owners sought damages for a taking of land along a state highway as a result of runoff water discharged onto their property. The state's defense was that the property had been acquired by the state either through prescription or through the operation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1861(B). The property owners claimed that the statute was only curative or, in the alternative, was unconstitutional. After the trial court granted partial summary judgment to the property owners, a division of the court of appeals issued an opinion in another case stating that § 28-1861(B) was constitutional and that it transferred title to roadways to the state as a result of longstanding public use. The state then filed a special action with the court after the trial court declined to reconsider its partial summary judgment. The court agreed with the trial court and denied relief to the state. The court held that 1) Arizona law did not permit the creation of public highways by prescription and, therefore, the property owners did not lose their rights before the enactment of the statute; 2) the statute did not alter the common law; and 3) the statute was curative only.


OUTCOME: The court ruled that the state had not acquired title to the land either through prescription or through the operation of statute. The court held that the trial court's ruling was correct, accepted jurisdiction of the special action, and denied relief to the state.

State v. Lopez


No. CR-90-0247-AP


Supreme Court of Arizona

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted him of first degree murder and other offenses, and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and other offenses. The trial court sentenced him to death, and defendant sought review. The court held that a victim need not have been physically tortured for a murder to be especially cruel, and stated that a murder was especially cruel if the victim consciously experiences physical abuse or mental anguish before death. The court held that the victim had endured great suffering over a relatively protracted period of time while she struggled for her life and determined that her murder was cruel. The court further held that the crime was heinous and depraved because the victim was helpless and defendant inflicted gratuitous violence on her. Intoxication was only a mitigating factor under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-703(G)(1), if defendant's capacity to appreciate the wrongfulness of his conduct was significantly impaired, but not so impaired as to constitute a defense to prosecution. Under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-454(F), the court was allowed to consider any mitigating circumstances which were relevant. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of first degree murder and other offenses and sentenced him to death.

Defendant, who was 18 years old at the time of the murder, asserted 10 points of alleged error in his automatic appeal, including several challenges to the trial court's imposition of the death penalty. State v. Herrera


No. CR-89-0371-AP/PC


Supreme Court of Arizona


176 Ariz. 21; 859 P.2d 131; 1993 Ariz. LEXIS 30; 135 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 14



March 4, 1993

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted him of first degree felony murder, aggravated robbery, and kidnapping, and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree felony murder, aggravated robbery, and kidnapping, and was sentenced to death as a result of his involvement in the shooting of a police deputy. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that defendant's instruction to an accomplice to grab the deputy's gun while defendant was wrestling with the deputy was sufficient to establish defendant's liability for aggravated robbery. The court further determined that the murder of the deputy was in furtherance of the robbery pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1105(A)(2) because the murder prevented the deputy from regaining his gun. The court found that the murder conviction was properly premised on the kidnapping because the two crimes were not conceptually identical and did not occur as part of the same act. The court agreed with the trial judge's finding that defendant was an active participant in the murder based upon the fact that defendant shouted "shoot him" to encourage his accomplice to complete the crime. The court also determined that the death penalty was properly imposed because the deputy endured both physical abuse and unimaginable mental anguish before being shot.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction because there was substantial evidence to show that he was an active participant in the murder, robbery, and kidnapping of a police deputy. The court also affirmed the death sentence because the crime was committed in an especially cruel manner and the mitigating circumstances did not outweigh the aggravating circumstances.

Tucson Unified Sch. Dist. v. Owens-Corning Fiberglass Corp.


No. CV-92-0188-CQ


Supreme Court of Arizona


174 Ariz. 336; 849 P.2d 790; 1993 Ariz. LEXIS 20; 134 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



March 2, 1993 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration Denied; Clarification Granted and Opinion Amended May 7, 1993. *


*  Feldman, C.J., recused himself and did not participate in the determination of this matter. Fidel, C.J., was designated to sit in his stead.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] United States District Court No. CIV 87-975-TUC-WDB.

QUESTION OF LAW CERTIFIED BY THE UNITED STATES DISTRICT COURT FOR THE DISTRICT OF ARIZONA


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff school district filed a complaint in the United States District Court for the District of Arizona alleging that defendant corporations were liable for asbestos removal costs. After granting the school district's motion to strike the corporations' statute of limitations defense, the federal court certified to the court the question whether Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-510 precluded the corporations from interposing such a defense.


OVERVIEW: Upon both the school district's and the corporations' requests, the federal court certified the issue of whether § 12-510 exempted the school district from the statute of limitations. The court held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-529 suggested that political subdivisions were included within the ambit of § 12-510. By expressly stating in § 12-529 that statutes of limitations did apply to political subdivisions of the state in claims involving the navigability of watercourses, the legislature tacitly acknowledged that statutes of limitations did not apply to political subdivisions of the state in other types of cases. Moreover, the court held that the activities of the school district had not removed it from the protection of § 12-510. Under Arizona law, § 12-510 precluded the corporations from raising the statute of limitations as a legal defense to the suit by the school district.


OUTCOME: The court responded to the federal court's certified question, holding that the school district was protected from a statute of limitations defense.

State Comp. Fund v. Symington


No. CV-92-0243-SA


Supreme Court of Arizona


174 Ariz. 188; 848 P.2d 273; 1993 Ariz. LEXIS 15; 133 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 29



February 23, 1993 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Mandate Issued March 19, 1993.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State Compensation Fund (fund) filed a special action directly with the court seeking to have Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-987(1), (2), (3) declared unconstitutional. Those provisions amended requirements regarding the calculation of federal equivalency tax and also imposed an annual alternate minimum tax. The respondent state officials asserted the provisions' validity and urged the court's non-acceptance of special jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The court accepted special jurisdiction in this action to allow the state officials to take timely action regarding budgetary matters. The legislature adopted statutory amendments requiring the fund to retroactively pay an annual alternative minimum tax in an attempt to balance the state's budget. The fund asserted that the challenged provisions required a tax assessment and violated Arizona Constitution provisions. The court accepted jurisdiction over the special action and determined that the provisions requiring the alternative minimum tax were invalid because Ariz. Const. art. IV, pt. 2, § 19(9) provided that special legislation could not be enacted to assess or collect taxes. The court also found that there was no identified rational basis for the state legislature to have "singled out" the fund and that the discriminatory imposition of the tax did not rationally further the goal of balancing the state's budget. The federal equivalency tax was found to be not severable from the alternative minimum tax and was, therefore, also found to be invalid.


OUTCOME: The court enjoined the state officials from taking any actions to enforce the section the court found violative of the special legislative prohibition of the Arizona Constitution.

No. 1 CR-90-0142-AP

174 Ariz. 131; 847 P.2d 1078; 1992 Ariz. LEXIS 101; 129 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



December 22, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration Denied March 31, 1993.

Habeas corpus proceeding at, Remanded by Lopez v. Schriro, 2007 U.S. App. LEXIS 14470 (9th Cir. Ariz., June 20, 2007)

State v. Salazar


No. CR-88-0135-AP/PC


Supreme Court of Arizona


173 Ariz. 399; 844 P.2d 566; 1992 Ariz. LEXIS 100; 128 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 10



December 17, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Mandate Issued. As Corrected March 25, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Pima County No. CR-19301. Appeal and Petition for Review from the Superior Court of Pima County. The Honorable Gilbert Veliz, Jr., Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder, kidnapping, and first degree burglary and was sentenced to death for the murder. He filed a petition for post-conviction relief alleging ineffective assistance of counsel at trial and sentencing, The Superior Court of Pima County, Arizona, denied the petition. Defendant's petition to review that ruling was consolidated with the appeal of his murder conviction, which was automatic.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court found that: (1) a criminalist was not an undeclared witness because the defense counsel overlooked her report in his pretrial preparation; (2) defendant failed to demonstrate the probability that his trial was unfair when he argued that his trial was tainted by publicity before and during his trial; (3) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting a photograph of the victim where it was introduced to aid the medical examiner's testimony and was probative on the issue of intent: (4) a detective's footprint testimony was admissible because he had been trained in tracking and had investigated numerous burglarized premises to determine points of entry; (5) the trial court's rejection of expert testimony on the effects of intoxication was proper because such knowledge was within the common knowledge and experience of the jury; (6) the jury was properly instructed; and (7) a first-degree murder verdict is not constitutionally deficient unless there is a unanimous jury finding on a single theory of first degree murder. The court did not conduct a separate proportionality review in this case and will not conduct them in future cases.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of conviction and the sentences of the trial court. The court found no fundamental error. The court also held that it would no longer conduct proportionality reviews in death penalty cases.

State v. Tober


No. CR-91-0375-PR


Supreme Court of Arizona


173 Ariz. 211; 841 P.2d 206; 1992 Ariz. LEXIS 91; 125 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 17



November 3, 1992

Rios v. Symington


No. CV-92-0129-SA


Supreme Court of Arizona


172 Ariz. 3; 833 P.2d 20; 1992 Ariz. LEXIS 48; 116 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



June 30, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Mandate Issued July 16, 1992. As Corrected September 22, 1992.



DISPOSITION: Relief granted in part and denied in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the governor exercised line-item veto on two legislative bills and instructed various state agencies to revert specified sums of money to the general fund to bring the total budget in line with the governor's projected revenues, petitioner President of the Arizona Senate filed a special action directly to the court seeking a judicial declaration the governor's vetoes and reversion orders were invalid.


OVERVIEW: Upon presentation of two house bills, a fund transfer bill and an amendment of general appropriations, the governor signed the bills, but exercised his line item veto power, and also ordered agencies to revert money to the general fund. The senate president filed an action with the court, seeking a declaration that the vetoes and reversion orders were invalid. The court held that (1) the special funds at issue were appropriations, as the legislature set aside a certain sum of money for a specified object and created an authority to spend that money, so that the transfer of funds to the general fund constituted appropriations subject to line item veto, (2) the veto of statutorily seized funds was invalid because the statute did not amount to an appropriation, (3) the line item veto of an amended appropriation was valid where it rendered the amendment void, and the amount appropriated in the original appropriations bill still stood, and (4) the reversions were unconstitutional because the governor vetoed the line items, but then replaced them with his own amount, which usurped the legislature's powers.


OUTCOME: The court held that special funds, as appropriations, were subject to line item veto, but that statutorily seized funds were not subject to such veto, as they were not an appropriation. The line item veto of an amended appropriation was valid where the original appropriations bill still stood. The reversion orders were unconstitutional because the governor attempted to replace the legislature's funding bill with his own amount.

Ariz. Corp. Comm'n v. Ariz. ex rel. Woods


No. CV-91-0082-SA


Supreme Court of Arizona


171 Ariz. 286; 830 P.2d 807; 1992 Ariz. LEXIS 33; 111 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 5



April 21, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration Denied June 16, 1992.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] RELIEF GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, the Arizona Corporation Commission (commission) and commissioners, filed a special action that alleged that respondent state attorney general failed to perform a duty required by § 41-1041 of Arizona's Administrative Procedure Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-1041, when he refused to certify certain rules proposed by petitioner commission. The underlying issue was the scope of petitioner commission's power under Ariz. Const. art. 15, § 3.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, the Arizona Corporation Commission (commission) and commissioners, proposed rules that required intervenor public service corporations to report information about and obtain permission for transactions with their parents, subsidiaries, and other affiliated corporations. Respondent state attorney general refused to certify the rules. Petitioners brought a special action in which they claimed that respondent thereby failed to perform a duty required by § 41-1041 of Arizona's Administrative Procedure Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-1041. The court held that respondent violated § 41-1041 because Ariz. Const. art. 15, § 3 gave petitioner commission the authority to promulgate the proposed rules. The court found that petitioner commission had "full power" under the constitution to regulate, set rates, and make reasonable rules for public service companies. The court held that the proposed rules were reasonably connected to and necessary for petitioner commission's constitutional exclusive ratemaking power and were within its discretionary authority. The court also held that the proposed rules did not violate the federal Commerce Clause under U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3.


OUTCOME: The court held that respondent state attorney general failed to perform a duty required by law when he refused to certify certain rules proposed by petitioners, the Arizona Corporation Commission (commission) and commissioners. The court said that under the Arizona Constitution, petitioner commission had the authority to promulgate the proposed rules under its ratemaking power. The court directed respondent to certify the proposed rules.

 

98 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Noble


Supreme Court No. CR-91-0049-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


171 Ariz. 171; 829 P.2d 1217; 1992 Ariz. LEXIS 34; 111 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 17



April 21, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Mandate Issued May 12, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Court of Appeals No. 1 CA-CR 88-1281. Maricopa County No. CR 88-04973. Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. The Honorable Jeffrey S. Cates, Judge. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, 167 Ariz. 440, 808 P.2d 325 (Ct. App. 1990). vacated.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two defendants pled guilty to sex offenses that occurred before the effective date of the sex offender registration statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3821, and each was ordered to register. One panel of the Court of Appeals (Arizona) determined that the application was an ex post facto law and reversed it. Another panel determined that registration did not violate the ex post facto clause. The state and the second defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants in the consolidated cases committed conduct prior to the enactment of the sex offender registration statute but entered guilty pleas after its effective date. The trial courts, as part of the sentences, ordered registration under the statute. One panel of the court of appeals held that the application of the registration requirement to crimes predating its enactment violated the ex post facto clause of the Arizona Constitution. A different panel of the court of appeals held that registration as a sex offender for offenses committed before the enactment of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3821 did not violate the ex post facto clause. The court granted review in both cases to resolve the conflict between the two decisions. The court determined that § 13-3821 had the primary purpose of enabling law enforcement personnel to locate child sexual offenders. Although there were punitive results, the statute was regulatory in nature and was not an unconstitutional ex post facto law when applied to defendants who were convicted after the enactment of the statute for offenses predating the enactment of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court determined, on balance, that requiring convicted sex offenders to register pursuant to the statute was not punishment. Consequently, the retrospective application of the statute to defendants did not violate the ex post facto clauses of the United States or Arizona Constitutions. Therefore, the court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals that held that the statute did not violate the ex post facto clauses.

State v. Atwood

Supreme Court of Arizona


171 Ariz. 576; 832 P.2d 593; 1992 Ariz. LEXIS 29; 110 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Pima County Superior Court Nos. CR-14065 and CR-15397. Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County. (Trial held in Maricopa County). The Honorable John G. Hawkins, Judge * 


* The trial judge is now deceased.


Hoskinson ex rel. Fleming v. State of California, 168 Ariz. 250, 812 P.2d 1068, 1990 Ariz. App. LEXIS 401 (Ariz. Ct. App., Dec. 13, 1990)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions and the imposition of the death penalty in the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) for kidnapping and first-degree felony murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a previously convicted pedophile, allegedly abducted an eight-year-old girl and took her to the desert, where he molested and murdered her. There was sufficient evidence to support the kidnapping conviction: defendant's car was spotted at the intersection where the girl was abducted, paint from the girl's bike was on defendant's car, eyewitnesses saw the girl in his car, and his letters revealed his sexual attraction to young children. Additionally, even though the skeletal remains of the girl, discovered long after her disappearance, did not reveal a cause of death, the extensive circumstantial evidence was sufficient to satisfy the corpus delicti requirement and to support the murder conviction. Defendant failed to show that his counsel's conduct was insufficient or unreasonable, and he did not establish that he was prejudiced by any alleged errors. The death penalty statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-703, was constitutional and there were no mitigating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed.

State of Arizona v. Richard Michael Rossi


No. CR-88-0302-AP


Supreme Court of Arizona


171 Ariz. 276; 830 P.2d 797; 1992 Ariz. LEXIS 26; 109 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 22



April 2, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration Denied May 19, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Maricopa County No. CR-135863. Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. The Honorable Philip W. Marquardt, Judge (Retired)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an automatic appeal under Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-4033 and Ariz. R. Crim. P. 26.15, 31.2(b), defendant appealed an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which following remand, imposed the death penalty for first-degree murder. Three prior reviews upheld all of defendant's convictions and sentences expect for the death penalty that was imposed on the murder count.


OVERVIEW: Defendant robbed and murdered the victim in his home and injured a neighbor who tried to help. After two reviews, the court remanded and directed the trial court to consider at the sentencing the two additional mitigating circumstances of defendant showing that he was capable of rehabilitation and that the drug addiction significantly impaired his capacity to conform his conduct to the law's mandates. The trial court resentenced defendant to death and on appeal, the court affirmed. First, the mitigating factors were not sufficiently substantial to call for leniency. Second, a finding of a mitigating circumstance under Ariz. Rev. Stat. §13-703(G)(1) did not negate the finding of an aggravating circumstance under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-703(F)(6). Third, Arizona's death penalty was constitutional because proportionality reviews were not constitutionally mandated, it was not unconstitutional to allow the judge, not the jury, to determine the existence of aggravating and mitigating circumstances, and the statute provided constitutionally adequate standards to guide sentencing discretion. Fourth, double jeopardy or collateral estoppel did not bar reimposition of the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the imposition of the death penalty for defendant for his first-degree murder conviction.

In re the Rights ex rel. Gila River


No. WC-90-0001-IR


Supreme Court of Arizona


171 Ariz. 230; 830 P.2d 442; 1992 Ariz. LEXIS 25; 109 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



March 19, 1992  
March 19, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Mandate, April 15, 1992.
Remanded by In re General Adjudication of All Rights to Use Water in Gila River Sys. & Source, 175 Ariz. 382, 857 P.2d 1236, 1993 Ariz. LEXIS 60 (Ariz., 1993)
Related proceeding at In re General Adjudication of All Rights to Use Water in the Gila River Sys. & Source, 195 Ariz. 411, 989 P.2d 739, 1999 Ariz. LEXIS 116 (Ariz., 1999)
Related proceeding at In re General Adjudication of All Rights to Use Water in the Gila River Sys. & Source, 201 Ariz. 307, 35 P.3d 68, 2001 Ariz. LEXIS 205 (Ariz., 2001)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by In re General Adjudication of All Rights to use water in the Gila River system & source, 2006 Ariz. LEXIS 19 (Ariz., Feb. 9, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Maricopa County No. W-1, W-2, W-3, W-4 (Consolidated)
United States v. Superior Court, 144 Ariz. 265, 697 P.2d 658, 1985 Ariz. LEXIS 162 (Ariz., 1985)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner water user associations filed an interlocutory appeal to determine whether the procedures adopted by the trial court (Arizona) for service of summons and filing and service of pleadings in an underlying general water rights adjudication comported with due process under the Fourteenth Amendment and Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 4.


OVERVIEW: The consolidated action combined an adjudication of water rights for several areas in the state. On review, the court found that: (1) as the Arizona State Land Department (SLD) and the Arizona Department of Water Resources (DWR) sent notice via certified mail to over 849,000 property owners in the affected areas, they exercised due diligence in trying to ascertain the whereabouts of potential claimants, and notice by publication satisfied due process for property owners they had not located; (2) publication by notice satisfied due process for lienholders as requiring the SLD and the DWR to notice them by mail would have been an unreasonable burden; (3) publication of notice was proper for lessees and permit holders; (4) the summons adequately informed potential claimants of the nature of the proceedings; (5) filing and service provisions in the pretrial order were well-designed under the circumstances to afford litigants adequate notice of all filings in the adjudication; (6) the trial court had the authority to adopt the special procedures under Ariz. R. Civ. P. 16.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that the procedures adopted by the trial court for summons, filing, and service of pleadings in an underlying general water rights adjudication comported with due process under the Fourteenth Amendment and the Arizona Constitution.

State v. Brewer


Nos. CR-88-0308-AP, CR-89-0319-T/AP


Supreme Court of Arizona


170 Ariz. 486; 826 P.2d 783; 1992 Ariz. LEXIS 17; 106 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



January 28, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration Denied April 8, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Superior Court of Coconino County. The Honorable H. Jeffrey Coker, Judge. Coconino County CR-13470 & CR-13547



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his first-degree murder conviction and death sentence from the Superior Court of Coconino County (Arizona). Defendant pleaded guilty to the murder of his girlfriend. This automatic appeal followed under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4033. The state challenged the trial court's dismissal of the first-degree murder charge for the death of the victim's 22-week-old, unborn fetus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant brutally murdered his girlfriend and her 22-week-old, unborn fetus. Thereafter, defendant pleaded guilty to first-degree murder and was sentenced to death. An automatic appeal followed pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4033. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to conclude that defendant's ability to make rational choices and to understand the attendant consequences was not substantially impaired at the time of the guilty plea. Additionally, the court believed that defendant lacked any true sense of remorse for his crime. Also, having considered all the mitigation evidence, the court found that it was not sufficiently substantial to require leniency in light of the shocking cruelty of the defendant's crime; the death penalty was warranted. Having found no fundamental error pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4035, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and his sentence of death.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction upon defendant's plea of guilty to first-degree murder and the sentence of death. The court also affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the first-degree murder charge for the death of the fetus.

State v. Greenway

DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from a decision of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which convicted appellant of two counts of first degree murder, one count of first degree burglary, one count of theft by control, one count of arson of an unoccupied structure, and sentenced appellant to death.


OVERVIEW: The trial court sentenced appellant to death sentences for first degree murder, burglary, theft, and arson. 105 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Dietz v. General Elec. Co.


No. CV-90-0435-CQ


Supreme Court of Arizona


169 Ariz. 505; 821 P.2d 166; 1991 Ariz. LEXIS 121; 100 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 9



November 21, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Prior report: 167 Ariz. 439, 808 P.2d 324.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, injured employee and family, brought a negligence action in Pima County Superior Court (Arizona), against defendant electric companies. The electric companies named the employer as a nonparty at fault. The injured employee then brought a motion to strike the designation of the employer as a nonparty at fault.


OVERVIEW: The injured employee argued that under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-2501(H), an employer liable for workers' compensation could not be considered a nonparty at fault. The court held that the later enacted provisions of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-2506(B), which compelled the assessment of nonparty fault regardless of whether the nonparty was or could have been made a defendant to the action, prevailed over the provision in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-2501(H), which prohibited assessment against immune employers. The court held that the construction given to the statutes did not violate the Ariz. Const. art 2, § 31, and art. 18, § 6, which prohibited abrogation of a cause of action for injury and prohibited limitations on the amount of damages to be recovered for causing death or injury to any person. The court held that the injured employee was effectively prevented from recovering damages against his employer because he had already recovered from the employer under the workers' compensation law.


OUTCOME: The court answer the certified question and held that when an employer negligently contributed to an employee's injury, the joint tortfeasors may require the employer's negligence to be considered for the assessment of fault under state statutes. The court left the assessment of costs to the discretion of the district judge.

McDONALD v. CAMPBELL


No. CV-91-0024-PR


Supreme Court of Arizona


169 Ariz. 478; 821 P.2d 139; 1991 Ariz. LEXIS 116



October 22, 1991 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, the State of Arizona Personnel Board (board) and employee, sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Arizona), in favor of the state supreme court and its administrative director, that held that the court's motion to dismiss the employee's complaint should have been granted because the board did not have jurisdiction to hear complaints filed by court employees.


OVERVIEW: After the employee was discharged from her position with the state supreme court, she filed a complaint with the board. The state supreme court and its administrative director filed a motion to dismiss, arguing that the board did not have jurisdiction to consider whistle blowing complaints involving court employees. The board denied the motion. Thereafter, the state supreme court and its administrative director filed a complaint with the trial court seeking an order directing the board to dismiss the employee's complaint. The trial court denied the relief requested. The lower court held that the motion to dismiss should have been granted. On appeal, the court held that by enacting Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 38-532(I), the legislature attempted to grant the board the right to directly interfere with the court's administrative decisions concerning the tenure of employees. That interference was contrary to Ariz. Const. art. 6, § 7, and the statute was unconstitutional. The lower court correctly concluded that the board lacked jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the trial court with directions that the employee's wrongful discharge complaint filed with the board be dismissed.

Rotter v. Coconino County


No. CV-90-0327-PR


Supreme Court of Arizona


169 Ariz. 269; 818 P.2d 704; 1991 Ariz. LEXIS 115; 96 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



October 3, 1991 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hotel owner filed suit after defendant county denied his permit to expand his nonconforming use onto adjacent tracts of land. The trial court found the expansion was permissible, which the county appealed. The appellate court (Arizona) affirmed, and the county appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county contended it was authorized to regulate nonconforming uses of land within its boundaries. The court held that (1) Coconino County, Ariz. Ordinance § 17.3(B) complied with Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 11-830(A), which restricted a county's authority to regulate nonconforming uses, (2) statutory amendments indicated that the legislature intended to distinguish between the absolute right of a nonconforming business use to continue in its present state and the limited right of a nonconforming use to reasonable expansion, (3) § 11-830(B) did not give a nonconforming use an absolute right to expand up to one hundred percent free of any regulation by the commission, and (4) a nonconforming use on one lot did not permit the owner to expand the use onto the owner's adjoining lots that were acquired after the ordinance was passed.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the appellate court's opinion, reversed the judgment, and remanded the case with instructions to enter judgment in favor of the county.

Neal v. Kingman


No. CV-90-0490-PR


Supreme Court of Arizona


169 Ariz. 133; 817 P.2d 937; 1991 Ariz. LEXIS 72; 95 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 6



September 17, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 18, 1991. Mandate Issued October 8, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Mohave County; No. C-25441; The Honorable Michael Irwin, Judge.

Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, No. 1 CA-CV-88-268;    Ariz.   ,    P.2d    (App. 1990), VACATED IN PART.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sign owner appealed a decision by a city zoning administrator (city), that a sign he had erected was not properly oriented, to the city board of adjustment (board), which affirmed the city. The superior court affirmed the board, but held that the sign owner had raised a vested rights issue before the board and ordered a trial de novo. The Court of Appeals (Arizona) affirmed. The city sought review.


OVERVIEW: The city had determined that a sign the sign owner had erected did not conform with Kingman, Ariz., Zoning Ord. 135, § XXV, Off-Premise Sign, § 5, in that it was not properly oriented to the road on the zoning request. The sign owner was not represented before the board and his appeal only addressed the issue of orientation. In reversing the court of appeals, the court noted that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 9-462.06(D) required that a person seeking review of a decision of a zoning administrator file a notice of appeal specifying the grounds thereof. While the statute did not require that the notice of appeal specify the precise legal theory or theories upon which an appellant relied, it must, in some fashion, give fair notice of what would be challenged on appeal. The court held that by failing to assert a vested rights issue in his notice of appeal or otherwise, the sign owner had waived that issue. Once the trial court concluded that the board had not abused its discretion in upholding the city's decision concerning the orientation of the sign, the case should have ended.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the appeals court and remanded to the trial court with directions to enter judgment affirming the board.

State v. Lavers


Supreme Court No. CR-89-0298-AP


Supreme Court of Arizona


168 Ariz. 376; 814 P.2d 333; 1991 Ariz. LEXIS 59; 91 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 38



July 23, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Mandate Issued August 13, 1991. Motion for Issuance of Warrant of Execution Granted February 4, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; No. CR-88-10549; The Honorable Cheryl Hendrix, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted defendant of two counts of first degree murder and imposed two death sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of first degree murder after he killed his wife and daughter. The trial court imposed two death sentences and defendant sought review. He alleged multiple errors from the admission of an audio tape made by defendant's daughter during the attack, and alleged other errors. The court affirmed, finding that it was not necessary for police officers to obtain a separate search warrant for the tape when the warrant's scope included all evidence that pertained to the murder. The tape was properly admitted because a proper foundation was laid and because the trial court, in the exercise of its judicial discretion, was satisfied that the recording was accurate, authentic, and generally trustworthy. The tape did not violate defendant's right to confrontation because the declarant was unavailable and the statements were reliable under the circumstances. Imposition of the death sentence was proper because the record showed that defendant committed the murders in an especially heinous, cruel, or depraved manner. Cruelty was established because the record showed that defendant inflicted mental anguish or physical abuse before the victims died.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's murder convictions and death sentences.

State v. White


Supreme Court No. CR-88-0287-AP


Supreme Court of Arizona


168 Ariz. 500; 815 P.2d 869; 1991 Ariz. LEXIS 57; 91 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 19



July 16, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Mandate Issued July 16, 1991. Motion to Set Date of Execution GRANTED; Warrant of Execution signed May 5, 1992.
Writ of certiorari denied White v. Arizona, 502 U.S. 1105, 112 S. Ct. 1199, 117 L. Ed. 2d 439, 1992 U.S. LEXIS 1356 (1992)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. White, 194 Ariz. 344, 982 P.2d 819, 1999 Ariz. LEXIS 80 (Ariz., 1999)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Stay denied by, Stay lifted by, Motion denied by, As moot White v. Ryan, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 64032 (D. Ariz., July 13, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Yavapai County; No. 12855; The Honorable James Hancock.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant and his lover conspired to and did murder the lover's husband in order to collect insurance proceeds. Defendant was convicted for first degree murder and conspiracy to commit murder by the Superior Court of Yavapai County, Arizona. On a finding of the aggravating factor of a pecuniary motive, defendant was sentenced to death, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. 13-703(E). Defendant appealed from the conviction and the sentence.


OVERVIEW: In affirming the order of conviction and sentence, the court rejected the claim that the trial court erred in instructing the jury, holding that 1) it was the trial court's duty to determine the existence of a conspiracy, so defendant's proposed instruction was incorrect, 2) for the same reason, defendant was not denied a jury trial on the conspiracy issue, and 3) the trial court correctly denied defendant's proposed instruction on the jury's role in determining the admissibility of co-conspirator's statements. In addition, the conspiracy did not end at the murder, but embraced the collection of the insurance proceeds, so the lover's statements after the murder fell within the co-conspirator hearsay exception. Although the admission of defendant's bigamy was error, it was not prejudicial. The court found that, because defendant's sentence was death for murder, there was no double punishment under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-116. Finally, the court found there was no error or unconstitutionality in the imposition of the death sentence, because Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-703(E) mandates death for a murder with aggravating circumstances, not balanced by mitigating factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order of conviction and sentence against defendant, on the charges of first degree murder and conspiracy to commit murder.

W. Devcor v. Scottsdale


Supreme Court No. CV-91-0116-AP


Supreme Court of Arizona


168 Ariz. 426; 814 P.2d 767; 1991 Ariz. LEXIS 54; 91 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 10



July 11, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Mandate Issued August 2, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; No. CV 91-00902; The Honorable Colin F. Campbell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which found in favor of appellee city and intervenor voters when it upheld the validity of petitions and permitted a referendum election in an action concerning the rezoning of the owner's property.


OVERVIEW: The city unanimously approved the rezoning of the owner's property. The voters intervened and filed a referendum petition seeking to refer the city's decision to the voters. The owner filed suit seeking to prevent the referendum. The trial court ruled that the referendum petitions were sufficient and that the matter should be submitted to the city's voters. On review, the court reversed. The petitions did not comply with Ariz. Const. art. 4, pt. 1, § 1(9) and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 19-112(B), and the defect was not cured. The petitions were insufficient to require an election. Because the referendum was an "extraordinary" power, that permitted a minority to hold up the effective date of legislation that could represent the wishes of the majority, the Arizona Supreme Court required referendum proponents to comply strictly with applicable constitutional and statutory provisions. The circulators' affidavits failed to state, as both Ariz. Const. art. 4, pt. 1, § 1(9) and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 19-112(B) specifically required, that the circulators believed each signer to be a qualified elector of the city.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and directed it to enter judgment in favor of the owner because the voter's petitions were insufficient to require an election by the city.

In re Wade


Supreme Court No. SB-90-0013-D


Supreme Court of Arizona


168 Ariz. 412; 814 P.2d 753; 1991 Ariz. LEXIS 51; 90 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



July 3, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Mandate Issued July 24, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Disciplinary Commission No. 5-2173.



DISPOSITION: DISCIPLINARY PROCEEDINGS RESPONDENT SUSPENDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent attorney sought review of a decision by the state bar association's disciplinary committee (Arizona), which affirmed a hearing committee's recommendation to suspend the attorney's license for two years and to pay restitution and the cost of the proceedings. The court had original jurisdiction under Ariz. Sup. Ct. R. 53(e). Ariz. Code of Prof'l Responsibility R. 29(a), not Ariz. Rules of Prof'l Conduct R. 42, was applicable.


OVERVIEW: The attorney was found to have violated the state's ethical code by a hearing committee who recommended certain sanctions, which were affirmed by the disciplinary commission. The attorney appealed. The court had original jurisdiction, affirmed the commission's decision, and held that: (1) the attorney violated Ariz. Code of Prof'l Responsibility DR 5-104 because there was a conflict of interest with a client and the attorney did not properly advise his client of the conflict or of the client's right to consult another attorney, which was not lessened by the fact that the client was not harmed and justified the commission's two year suspension; (3) the attorney violated Ariz. Code of Prof'l Responsibility DR 9-102 because he did not preserve the identity of funds and property of a client but the commission's two-year probation was insufficient and the court imposed an additional two year suspension; (3) because the attorney actively frustrated restitution for his client, and because of the manner in which the attorney contested this matter, the suspensions ran consecutively; and (4) the attorney was entitled to be represented by counsel but not appointed counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the findings of the commission but changed the sanction from a two year suspension to a four year suspension. The court ordered that the attorney pay costs, restitution, and a fine for violation of appellate rules.

State v. Western


Supreme Court No. CR-90-0228-PR


Supreme Court of Arizona


168 Ariz. 169; 812 P.2d 987; 1991 Ariz. LEXIS 65; 89 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3; 59 U.S.L.W. 2771



May 30, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Mandate Issued May 30, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; The Honorable Michael J. O'Melia, Judge; Court of Appeals No. 1 CA-CR 89-048; Maricopa County No. LCA 88-00574; Memorandum Decision of the Court of Appeals, Division One, filed June 12, 1990, vacated.



DISPOSITION: VACATED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) that convicted her of violating Scottsdale, Ariz. Rev. Code § 16-242 (1987).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested while dancing partially clothed at a nightclub. She was convicted of violating § 16-242, which prohibited certain forms of striptease. A striptease was defined in § 16-236 as a performance in which a person appeared in various degrees of undress. Defendant appealed, and the court vacated her conviction, finding § 16-242 and the applicable definitional sections unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. Section 16-242 was vague because it did not give fair warning to persons as to what attire and movements were prohibited. There was no standard for determining what "various degrees of undress" contemplated. Further, § 16-242 was overbroad because it infringed upon First Amendment rights. It impermissibly regulated non-obscene dancing at locations that did not serve alcohol.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment that convicted defendant of violating a local ordinance that prohibited stripteasing.

 

114 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stanley


No. CR-87-0289-AP


Supreme Court of Arizona


167 Ariz. 519; 809 P.2d 944; 1991 Ariz. LEXIS 13; 82 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



February 7, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected February 14, 1991. Mandate Issued May 17, 1991.
Writ of certiorari denied Stanley v. Arizona, 502 U.S. 1014, 112 S. Ct. 660, 116 L. Ed. 2d 751, 1991 U.S. LEXIS 7193 (1991)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Stay vacated by Stanley v. Schriro, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 71355 (D. Ariz., Sept. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Yavapai County; No. 11909; The Honorable James B. Sult, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the Superior Court of Yavapai County (Arizona) of two counts of first degree murder. Defendant was sentenced to death for killing his daughter and to life imprisonment for killing his wife. Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences.


OVERVIEW: The court held that defendant was not in custody at the time of his confession and that even though defendant invoked his right to decline further interrogation until he had spoken to a lawyer, the police were entitled to continue to question him because it was a non-custodial setting. The court rejected defendant's contention that the magistrate who issued the search warrant was not neutral and detached because he went to the crime scene to sign the warrant. The court found that under the unique circumstances of the case there was no error. The court noted, however, that normally it did not approve of magistrates visiting crime scenes. The court agreed with the trial court's conclusion that defendant and his father voluntarily consented to the search and, therefore, it rejected defendant's challenge to the search on lack of consent grounds. The court rejected defendant's argument that he was deprived of a fair trial because it found that defendant failed to show either outrageous publicity or resulting prejudice from the media coverage. Finally, the court upheld the death sentence, finding that the murder of the child was committed in a particularly depraved manner.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

 

115 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Espinoza v. Superior Court


No. CV-90-0030-PR


Supreme Court of Arizona


166 Ariz. 557; 804 P.2d 90; 1991 Ariz. LEXIS 1; 77 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 18



January 3, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Mandate Issued January 25, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County; No. CR-28305; The Honorable Leslie Miller, Judge. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division Two; Filed November 21, 1989; No. 2 CA-SA 89-0130; Vacated.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state, a real party in interest, challenged a decision from the Court of Appeals (Arizona), which granted petitioner special action relief from an assessment of attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner received court-appointed counsel to defend her against a criminal charge. The magistrate ordered petitioner to pay $ 100 toward attorney's fees in $ 20 per month installments. Petitioner paid $ 60 of the assessment. Petitioner's counsel filed a motion to vacate the attorney's fee assessment, which was denied by the superior court. Petitioner was granted a special action relief by the court of appeals. The court reviewed the constitutionality of Ariz. R. Crim. P. 6.7(d). Under rule 6.7(d), petitioner was entitled to court-appointed counsel that was not state provided because she was considered to be quasi-indigent. Further, rule 6.7(d) authorized the court to order the petitioner to contribute to her defense costs. This type of order did not impair the petitioner's right to counsel. Moreover, the limitation imposed by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 11-584(B) did not restrict the court's authority to order partial payment of legal expenses by petitioner. If she felt that the amount assessed by the magistrate was unreasonable; petitioner was entitled to file a motion for reconsideration at the end of the proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the court of appeals' decision and affirmed the decision rendered by the trial court. It was not an abuse of discretion for the trial court to order petitioner to pay the amount she could afford to pay towards her defense.

 

116 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lyons


No. CR-90-0262-PR


Supreme Court of Arizona


167 Ariz. 15; 804 P.2d 744; 1990 Ariz. LEXIS 256; 76 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 27



December 18, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Mandate Issued December 18, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; No. CR-87-07223; The Honorable Ronald S. Reinstein, Judge.

Memorandum Decision of the Court of Appeals; Division One, Filed June 12, 1990; No. 1 CA-CR 89-1578-PR; Approved in Part; Vacated in Part.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to two counts of attempted child molestation. Defendant was sentenced to lifetime supervised probation on the first count and to a mitigated term of imprisonment on the second count. The Court of Appeals (Arizona) remanded the case to consider the validity of imposing lifetime probation under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604.01(I). The state petitioned the court to determine the constitutionality of the provision.


OVERVIEW: The court noted that although it had previously determined that imposing lifetime parole unconstitutionally violated separation of powers, the power to make decisions regarding probation was solidly within the scope of the judiciary's authority. The court said that unlike the lifetime parole provision, which impermissibly created an intertwining of judicial and executive powers, the lifetime probation provision caused no such overlap. Accordingly, the court found that § 13-604.01(I) did not violate the separation of powers doctrine. Similarly, the court held that § 13-604.01(I) was not unconstitutionally vague. The court said that unlike the lifetime parole provision, under which the penalty for violating parole was uncertain, the penalty for violating probation was revocation, modification, or continuation of probation. The court concluded that § 13-604.01(I) was constitutional and valid. Therefore, it vacated that portion of the intermediate court's order that remanded the matter to the trial court. The court affirmed the trial court's order.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the remand portion of the intermediate court's order. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction, sentence, and lifetime probation.

State v. Fierro


No. CR-87-0051-AP


Supreme Court of Arizona


166 Ariz. 539; 804 P.2d 72; 1990 Ariz. LEXIS 260; 76 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 12



December 18, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 15, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; No. CR-153626; The Honorable Stephen A. Gerst, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as Modified


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of first-degree murder and first-degree burglary. The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) sentenced defendant to death for the murder and to life imprisonment, without the possibility of parole for 25 years, for the burglary. The court reviewed the judgment automatically pursuant to Ariz. Const. art. 6, § 5(3) and Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 13-4031, 13-4033.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was in the course of committing a burglary at a residence when the homeowners, a man and his fiancee, returned. The man jumped out of his car, armed with a gun, and confronted defendant. While the fiancee was talking on her car phone with an emergency operator, defendant shot the man in the chest. The man died from his wounds. Defendant was indicted on charges of first-degree murder, attempted murder, and burglary. The court held that (1) the fiancee's in-court identification of defendant was tainted by an unduly suggestive pre-trial identification procedure, but the identification was nonetheless admissible because it bore indicia of reliability and had a source independent of the pre-trial viewing, (2) the trial court did not err in admitting evidence of a prior burglary in area because the State presented substantial circumstantial evidence that defendant committed the burglary, (3) the trial court erred in using defendant's prior convictions for aggravated assault and robbery to establish the "prior felony involving violence " aggravating circumstance, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-703(F)(2), and (4) death sentence was disproportionate to penalty imposed in similar cases.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's murder conviction, reduced the death sentence to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole for at least 25 years, and ordered that his life sentence on the murder charge was to be served consecutively with his life sentence on the burglary charge.

State v. Amaya-Ruiz


No. CR-86-0095-AP/PC


Supreme Court of Arizona


166 Ariz. 152; 800 P.2d 1260; 1990 Ariz. LEXIS 228; 69 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 12



September 6, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 4, 1990. As Corrected Nunc Pro Tunc December 14, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County; Superior Court No. CR-15155; The Honorable Alice Truman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which convicted him of various crimes including first degree murder and manslaughter, and sentenced him to death on the murder conviction, and to a total of 19.5 years to run concurrently on the other convictions. Defendant also sought review of the denial of his petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of and sentenced for various crimes, including the first degree murder of a pregnant woman. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. Defendant first argued that he was incompetent to stand trial. The court disagreed, and held that the trial court adequately ensured defendant's competency, noting defendant's lack of cooperation with his counsel. The court also rejected defendant's argument that the trial court erred in denying his requests for continuances, as he failed to show prejudice resulting from the denials. Additionally, the court held that the trial court did not commit clear and manifest error in finding defendant's confession voluntary. However, the trial court's jury instruction regarding transferred intent was deemed erroneous. The court held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1103(A)(5) precluded the doctrine of transferred intent because it explicitly required two mental states, one toward the mother, and the other toward the unborn child. Because the court could not be sure whether the verdict was based on the incorrect instruction, defendant's manslaughter conviction was reversed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's manslaughter conviction was reversed and remanded for a determination as to whether an erroneous jury instruction affected the verdict, and the judgment below in all other respects was affirmed.

Republic Inv. Fund I v. Surprise


Nos. CV-89-0048-PR, CV-89-0172-PR


Supreme Court of Arizona


166 Ariz. 143; 800 P.2d 1251; 1990 Ariz. LEXIS 204; 66 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 30



July 31, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Superior Court of Maricopa County; The Honorable Alan S. Kamin, Judge (Maricopa County No. CV 87-09326); The Honorable J. D. Howe, Judge (Maricopa County No. CV 87-19086). Memorandum Decision of the Court of Appeals Division Two, 2 CA-CIV 88-0216, Filed November 15, 1988 Vacated. Opinion of the Court of Appeals Division One, 1 CA-CIV 88-100, Filed March 23, 1989 Approved.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted review of the decisions of the Court of Appeals Division Two (Arizona) and the Court of Appeals Division One (Arizona), which reached conflicting decisions in analyzing the constitutionality of the Arizona deannexation law, former Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 9-471. The statute was challenged as an allegedly prohibited special or local statute under Ariz. Const. art. 4, pt. 2, § 19(20).


OVERVIEW: Appellant municipalities argued that the deannexation statute was unconstitutional. The superior court upheld the statute in both actions, and one court of appeals affirmed, while the other reversed. The court found the statute unconstitutional. The statute, which was aimed at remedying problems stemming from abusive annexation practices, affected a limited class of cities for a limited period of time. The statute was, therefore, a special or local law. Although it was rationally related to a legitimate legislative goal, and it, therefore, satisfied the equal protection test, it did not meet the two special/local law standards. Namely, it did not apply uniformly to all members of the class, it was not elastic, it excluded similarly situated members of the class, and a general law could have been made applicable. As such, the deannexation statute violated Ariz. Const. art. 4, pt. 2, § 19(20). The remaining portions of the statute, however, were severable and remained in force.


OUTCOME: The court approved the judgment of the court of appeals, which found the statute unconstitutional. The court vacated the judgment of the second court of appeals, which found the statute constitutional.

State v. Comer

Supreme Court of Arizona

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from Maricopa County (Arizona), which found him guilty of murder, armed robbery, kidnapping, and other related charges, and which sentenced him to death.

OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions and the death sentence.

State v. Hinchey


No. CR-87-0317-AP


Supreme Court of Arizona


165 Ariz. 432; 799 P.2d 352; 1990 Ariz. LEXIS 206; 66 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 10



July 31, 1990 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial in an Arizona trial court, defendant was convicted of attempted first-degree murder and first-degree murder. The trial court sentenced defendant to 21 years imprisonment for the attempted murder conviction and to death for the murder conviction. Defendant sought review of his first-degree murder conviction and sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot the woman he had lived with for 12 years and killed her daughter. Defendant was charged with attempted murder and first-degree murder. The jury returned a verdict of guilty on both charges. The trial court imposed the death penalty. Defendant appealed. OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's first-degree murder conviction, vacated the sentence of death, and remanded the matter for resentencing.

Tucson v. Fahringer


No. CV-88-0469-PR


Supreme Court of Arizona


164 Ariz. 599; 795 P.2d 819; 1990 Ariz. LEXIS 199; 64 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 38



July 12, 1990  
July 12, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County; No. 228625; The Honorable Philip Fahringer, Judge. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division Two; No. 2 CA-SA-88-0072; 162 Ariz. 159, 781 P.2d 637 (Ct. App. 1988).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED; Vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured passengers, in their negligence action, appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which ruled in favor of defendants, city and state, and vacated a trial court order granting the injured passengers' motion to strike the city and state's affirmative defense of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-820.03(2). The trial court ruled that § 12-820.03(2) violated Ariz. Const. art. XVIII, § 6.


OVERVIEW: Injured passengers filed a negligence action against a city and state for injuries sustained in a car accident. The city and state alleged that the driver was intoxicated at the time of the accident, and raised Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-820.03(2), which protected public entities from liability to passengers driving with an intoxicated driver, as an affirmative defense. The injured passengers sought to strike the defense. The trial court declared § 12-820.03(2) unconstitutional. The city and state petitioned the court of appeals, which vacated the trial court's order, holding that § 12-820.03(2) was constitutional. The injured passengers appealed. The court found that § 12-820.03(2) was a legislative codification of the doctrine of contributory negligence because it provided an absolute bar to recovery of damages by a particular category of persons who otherwise could proceed with an action for damages. Because Ariz. Const. art. XVIII, § 5 prohibited either the trial judge or the legislature from interfering with a plaintiff's right to have a jury examine the existence or extent of contributory negligence, the court held that § 12-820.03(2) was unconstitutional and void.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the opinion of the court of appeals in favor of the city and state, affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the injured passengers, and remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Jonas

OVERVIEW: Defendant sold, for a nominal fee, a small amount of marijuana to a 14-year-old. The court found that counseling and incarceration proved useless and that defendant appeared unwilling to conform to society's rules.

In re Pima County Juvenile Appeal


No. CV-89-0159-PR


Supreme Court of Arizona


164 Ariz. 25; 790 P.2d 723; 1990 Ariz. LEXIS 61; 58 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



April 4, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County, Court of Appeals No. 2 CA-JV 89-0004, Pima County No. 74802-2, The Honorable Gilbert Veliz, Judge. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division Two, 162 Ariz. 97, 781 P.2d 74 (App. 1989), Approved.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner juvenile delinquent appealed from the Court of Appeals, Division Two (Arizona), which affirmed a juvenile court's revocation of the juvenile delinquent's probation based on a finding that he had sexually abused a 14-year-old girl, in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1404. The juvenile delinquent challenged the applicability of § 13-1404 to minors and argued that § 13-1404 was overly broad and vague.


OVERVIEW: A juvenile delinquent's probation was revoked upon a juvenile court's finding that the juvenile delinquent had touched the breasts of a 14-year-old girl. The juvenile court held that the sexual contact had constituted sexual abuse under § 13-1404, despite the girl's consent. The appellate court affirmed the revocation of the juvenile delinquent's probation. On further appeal, the court also affirmed. Specifically, the court rejected the juvenile delinquent's arguments that § 13-1404 was unconstitutionally vague or overly broad, holding that the statute was explicit and unambiguous in its language, provided clearly ascertainable standards of guilt, and did not promote arbitrariness. The court also held that the juvenile delinquent's constitutional right to privacy did not entitle him to engage in sexual contact with a partner under the age of 15, and thus § 13-1404 was not unconstitutional as applied. Finally, the court determined that the juvenile delinquent's policy arguments against application of § 13-1404 to juvenile defendants were matters within the legislature's, not the court's, purview.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision to uphold the revocation of the juvenile delinquent's probation. The court rejected the arguments that the sexual abuse law was unconstitutionally vague or overly broad or that it infringed on the right to privacy. The court also held that the policy arguments against application of the law to juvenile defendants were matters within the legislature's, not the court's, purview.
