CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court, Coconino County (Arizona), which convicted him of aggravated assault, kidnapping, sexual abuse, and sexual assault, all dangerous offenses committed while on parole. Defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment on each count with the sentences to run consecutively. On review, defendant challenged the circumstances of his arrest and the allegedly excessive sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of seven felony counts relating to abduction and rape, all offenses committed while he was on parole from prior convictions. Defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment and consecutive sentences. On appeal, defendant first alleged that the officer who arrested him did not have probable cause to do so. The court found that the officer had a detailed description of the crime and of defendant from the victim. This gave the officer sufficient information to believe that a crime was convicted and that defendant committed it. Defendant's Fourth Amendment rights were not compromised by the arrest. The court also rejected defendant's arguments that pretrial identification procedures, involving the victim's viewing a photographic lineup and observing defendant near the scene of the crime, were suggestive. The court found no abuse of discretion in the trial court's allowing testimony of an expert witness, a tracker, regarding shoe prints found close to where the victim was assaulted. The court held that the sentences were proper under the aggravating circumstances of the crimes and the improbability of defendant's rehabilitation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

State v. Phillips


No. CR-86-0256-PR


Supreme Court of Arizona


152 Ariz. 533; 733 P.2d 1116; 1987 Ariz. LEXIS 140



February 26, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima county, The Honorable Raner C. Collins, Judge Pro Tempore, Court of Appeals No. 2 CA-CR 4317, Pima County No. CR-15736.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AND SENTENCE VACATED REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Court of Appeals (Arizona), which affirmed his conviction and sentence for leaving the scene of an accident involving personal injury, a violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-661.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was driving home from work when a truck ahead of him slowed down to permit an elderly woman to cross the street. Unaware of the woman, defendant switched lanes to pass. He hit the woman, who suffered multiple injuries including a broken pelvis. Defendant panicked after hitting the woman and did not stop at the accident scene, but someone recorded his license number and gave it to the police. Defendant ultimately pled guilty to leaving the scene of an accident involving personal injury. He was placed on three years' probation and ordered to pay restitution to the victim. The appellate court affirmed, but the court vacated the judgment and remanded. The court concluded that defendant thoroughly understood the consequences of his agreement to pay restitution only if the record contained either a statement in the plea agreement setting forth a specific dollar amount, or a statement by defendant indicating agreement to pay a specific dollar amount, or a warning by the trial judge prior to accepting defendant's plea that he could order a specific dollar amount. Because the court found no such statements, it concluded that the trial court committed error.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's judgment and sentence and remanded.

Allen v. Industrial Comm'n


No. CV 86-0468-PR


Supreme Court of Arizona


152 Ariz. 405; 733 P.2d 290; 1987 Ariz. LEXIS 137



February 20, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Court of Appeals No. 1 CA-IC 3412, Special Action - Industrial Commission ICA Claim No. 454-62-6461, Carrier No. 029715, John B. Galloway, Administrative Law Judge.



DISPOSITION: AWARD AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee sought review of the decision of a court of appeals (Arizona), which affirmed an award of respondent Industrial Commission of Arizona (commission) that denied jurisdiction to hear the employee's workers' compensation claim because he failed to file his claim within one year as required by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1061(A).


OVERVIEW: The employee fell off a ladder during the course of his employment. The employee filed a claim beyond the one-year filing requirement outlined in § 23-1061(A). The commission found that it lacked jurisdiction to consider the claim for compensation because the claim had not been filed within the one-year period and because none of the statutory exceptions to the one-year filing requirement were available. The court rejected the employee's argument that § 23-1061(A) violated the constitution finding that because the statute provided the claimant with a reasonable opportunity to file a claim, one year after the injury occurred or the right thereto accrued, it did not violate the just and humane purposes of the constitutional amendment. The court held that the one-year filing requirement remained an affirmative defense which could have been waived. However, the court found that the employee did not timely file his claim within one year as required by § 23-1061(A) and the untimeliness of the claim was not waived. The court vacated the opinion of the court of appeals but affirmed the award.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the opinion of the court of appeals but affirmed the award.

State v. LaGrand


No. 6457


Supreme Court of Arizona


153 Ariz. 21; 734 P.2d 563; 1987 Ariz. LEXIS 133



January 30, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County, No. CR-07426, The Honorable J. Richard Hannah, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant and his half-brother were convicted by a jury of murder in the first degree, attempted murder in the first degree, attempted armed robbery, and two counts of kidnapping. The Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) sentenced defendant to death for the first degree murder and to concurrent terms of years for the other charges. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Two brothers attempted to rob a bank. One of the brothers, not the defendant appealing, confessed that he alone stabbed and killed the bank manager. The brother's confession was not admitted at trial because it was taken in violation of Miranda. The brothers and the state all stipulated to the voluntariness of the confession, but when defendant sought to have it admitted under Ariz. R. Evid. 804(b)(3), the state opposed and the statements were excluded as untrustworthy hearsay. The issues raised by defendant on appeal included the trial court's refusal to admit the brother's confession into evidence and the refusal to give a lesser included offense instruction regarding felony murder. The court found that the trial court did not limit its review of factors suggesting trustworthiness or lack thereof under Rule 804(b)(3) to evidence corroborating and contradicting the brother's statements. After reviewing such evidence, the court concluded that a reasonable person could not have found that the exculpatory statements were true. Because no lesser included offense to felony murder existed, it was not error to refuse the instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and his sentences for murder in the first degree, attempted murder in the first degree, attempted armed robbery, and two counts of kidnapping.

Boswell v. Phoenix Newspapers


No. 18159-PR


Supreme Court of Arizona


152 Ariz. 9; 730 P.2d 186; 1986 Ariz. LEXIS 312; 13 Media L. Rep. 1785



December 4, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Court of Appeals No. 1 CA-CIV 6123, Maricopa County Superior Court No. C-366121, The Honorable John H. Seidel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff defamed persons appealed a verdict in favor of defendants, newspaper and reporter, and that denied them general damages because the newspaper published a retraction of its defamatory article pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 12-653.02 and 12-653.03. The Superior Court of Maricopa County, Court of Appeals (Arizona) held that §§ 12.653.02 and 12-653.03 violated Ariz. Const. art. 18, § 6, and remanded the case. The newspaper appealed.


OVERVIEW: The newspaper published a conspicuous retraction after learning the original story was false. The trial judge instructed the jury that if the newspaper's retraction met the requirements of §§ 12.653.02 and 12.653.03, the jury could not have awarded general damages, which therefore precluded damages for loss of reputation and for emotional distress, which the defamed persons sought. Ariz. Const. art. 18, § 6 provided a right of action to recover damages for injuries that could never have been abrogated. The court concluded that § 6 was a strong open court provision that constitutionalized the right to access to the courts and a remedy for damages sustained, and protected the right to recover damages for injury to reputation. Section 6 was also not static, but evolved with the development of the common-law, and so also protected the right to seek recovery for emotional distress. The court found the retraction statutes violated § 6 because the statutes sought to abrogate recovery of damages for actual injury to reputation and for emotional suffering by completely depriving the defamed persons of a judicial remedy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the determination that the retraction statutes violated the constitutional provision that provided access to the courts for damages in defamation actions. The court reversed the jury's verdict and remanded the case for proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

Arizona Dep't of Revenue v. Trico Elec. Coop.


No. CV-86-0080-T


Supreme Court of Arizona


151 Ariz. 544; 729 P.2d 898; 1986 Ariz. LEXIS 298



November 19, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied January 13, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, The Honorable Thomas W. O'Toole, Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer corporation sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which reversed a decision by the state board of tax appeals (board), which reduced taxable value of the taxpayer corporation's property set by the state department of revenue (department), and assessed a 16 percent interest penalty. The court accepted transfer of the case from the court of appeals.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that the department's valuations as calculated under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-124.01(D), rather than the board's valuations as calculated under standard appraisal methods, reflected the proper cash value of the taxpayer corporation's property. The court found that the legislature intended the statutory formula in § 42-124.01 to be the exclusive method to calculate full cash value of electric and gas utilities. Because identical tax rates have been applied uniformly to both investor-owned and cooperative utility property, tax assessment discrepancies among utilities resulting from discretionary depreciation practices permitted by law did not violate Ariz. Const. art. 9, § 1 uniformity requirements. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-136(A)(2)(b) created two property classifications, one for electric and gas utilities and one for water and gas pipeline utilities. The court reversed the judgment that required the taxpayer corporation to pay 16 percent interest on the additional assessment resulting from reinstatement of the higher valuations, finding that the appropriate rate to be 10 percent under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-1201(A).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to accept the property valuation of the department but reversed the judgment that required the taxpayer corporation to pay 16 percent interest instead ordering the payment of 10 percent interest on the difference between the board's assessment and that of the trial court.

State v. Castaneda

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which convicted defendant of sexual conduct with a minor, kidnapping, and murder. Defendant was sentenced to death for first degree murder. Defendant presented issues of pretrial, trial, and post-trial allegations of error by the lower court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sexual conduct with a minor under 15, kidnapping, and first-degree murder and was sentenced to death for first-degree murder. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the trial court properly allowed defendant's admission of his prior convictions, that the circumstances of the murder indicated that the death penalty was properly imposed and that defendant's trial counsel was not ineffective.

State ex rel. Collins v. Superior Court


No. 18485-SA


Supreme Court of Arizona


150 Ariz. 295; 723 P.2d 644; 1986 Ariz. LEXIS 221



May 23, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Special Action Prayer for Relief Denied


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State of Arizona sought special action relief from a ruling by respondent Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3994(D) was unconstitutional. As a result of the superior court's ruling, the superior court denied the State's motion that defendant be confined after she was acquitted of attempted murder on grounds of insanity.


OVERVIEW: Following defendant's acquittal, the superior court made a finding pursuant to § 13-3994(D) that defendant's acts involved physical injury to the victim. The superior court also found that defendant was no longer a danger to herself or society. The court denied the special relief sought by the State, agreeing with the superior court that § 13-3994(D) was unconstitutional. Because § 13-3994(D) absolutely denied persons acquitted by reason of insanity the possibility of a release hearing to determine recovered sanity before 230 days had passed, the court held that § 13-3994(D) denied such persons due process of law. The court found that § 13-3994(D) contained no provision flexible enough to allow for evaluation or recovery before 230 days had elapsed. Further, the court found no legitimate governmental interest to outweigh the severe curtailment of liberty.


OUTCOME: The court denied the State's petition for special action relief from the superior court's ruling that a mandatory commitment statute was unconstitutional.

 

181 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Readenour v. Marion Power Shovel


No. 18224-PR


Supreme Court of Arizona


149 Ariz. 442; 719 P.2d 1058; 1986 Ariz. LEXIS 218; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P11,012



May 12, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Court of Appeals No. 2 CA-CIV 5183, Maricopa County No. C-439471, Honorable Robert W. Pickrell


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, worker and wife, brought a product liability action against defendant manufacturer for injuries suffered by the worker when he contacted high voltage conductors on an electrically powered mining shovel. The trial court entered judgment for the worker and wife. The Court of Appeals (Arizona) reversed the trial court's judgment. The worker and his wife appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the shovel was sold, the manufacturer modified the design to make the conductors less accessible. The worker and wife argued on appeal that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-686(2), limiting the use of design modification evidence, unconstitutionally infringed judicial rulemaking powers, or that § 12-686(2) was inapplicable. The manufacturer contended that the trial court erred either in admitting the evidence or in refusing a requested limiting instruction. The court held that § 12-686(2) was to be interpreted as forbidding, in a product liability action, the use of evidence of post-sale, pre-injury modification to prove a "defect" resulting from either negligent conduct or defective product quality, and that so interpreted, it was constitutional. The court determined that evidence of change to prove unreasonable danger was limited by both § 12-686(2) and Ariz. R. Evid. 407, but that the evidence could have been admitted for a number of other purposes. The court concluded that the refusal of the request for a limiting instruction was prejudicial error, because the lack of limiting instructions allowed the jury to use the evidence as an admission of defect or proof of negligent design.


OUTCOME: The court modified the opinion of the court of appeals, vacated the judgment, and remanded the case for a new trial and proceedings not inconsistent with the court's opinion.

 

182 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fletcher


No. 6374


Supreme Court of Arizona


149 Ariz. 187; 717 P.2d 866; 1986 Ariz. LEXIS 205



March 28, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County, The Honorable Richard N. Roylston, Judge, No. CR-117163


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Pima County Superior Court (Arizona) that convicted him of first degree murder and first degree burglary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's father helped defendant get a job at his company. After his father fired him, defendant shot and killed his father. Defendant claimed he was insane at the time of the crime. The order that convicted defendant of murder and burglary was affirmed. The court held that defendant's motion for mistrial was properly denied because the time the jury had spent in deliberations was not unreasonably long, a significant number of jurors had indicated that progress could be made on the burglary count, and a return of the jury for another day of deliberations did not work a hardship on any juror. The trial court erred in unilaterally modifying a supplemental jury instruction that had been agreed to by the parties. However, the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt because there was no proof that the modified supplemental instruction prejudiced defendant. Finally, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-502(B), which required defendant to prove with clear and convincing evidence that he was insane at the time of the crime, was constitutional. Because the burden of proof was a substantive matter, the legislature could have properly changed the burden of proof on the insanity defense.


OUTCOME: The order convicting defendant of first degree murder and first degree burglary was affirmed.

In re Appeal in Pima County Juvenile Action


No. 18524-PR


Supreme Court of Arizona


149 Ariz. 35; 716 P.2d 404; 1986 Ariz. LEXIS 302



March 17, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 29, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Juvenile Court of Pima County Cause No. J-70107-2, Honorable William L. Berlat, Judge Pro Tempore.Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division Two     Ariz.    ,     P.2d     (1985). Approved in Part; Vacated in Part, Court of Appeals No. 2 CA-Civ 5420.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant and the state appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals, Division Two (Arizona), which reversed a lower court's decision to transfer defendant from the juvenile court to the adult court for criminal processing based on the judge's fear that restitution could not be completed by defendant's 18th birthday.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a juvenile, was involved in a series of vehicle thefts and a delinquency petition was filed against him for theft and arson of property. The state filed a petition to transfer him to adult jurisdiction, and the lower court transferred him. Defendant appealed. The decision was vacated because the lower court transferred solely on a fear that restitution could not be completed by defendant's 18th birthday. Defendant and the state sought review. The court approved the vacation of the transfer order because Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-246, as amended, determined that age 18 was the limit of jurisdiction by a juvenile court, and the ability to complete restitution prior to loss of juvenile court jurisdiction was an improper basis upon which to transfer a juvenile to adult court. The court held that, even though defendant was no longer subject to jurisdiction of the juvenile court, he was not beyond the purview of the criminal justice system and the state could refile the charges in adult court because no determination was ever made whether he committed the acts alleged.


OUTCOME: The court approved the vacation of the transfer order in an action by the state to transfer defendant from juvenile court to adult criminal court prior to its loss of jurisdiction.

 

184 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Hall v. A.N.R. Freight Sys.


No. 18082-CQ


Supreme Court of Arizona


149 Ariz. 130; 717 P.2d 434; 1986 Ariz. LEXIS 194



March 12, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] QUESTIONS OF LAW CERTIFIED BY THE UNITED STATES DISTRICT COURT FOR THE DISTRICT OF ARIZONA, U.S. District Court No. CIV-84-691-TUC-RMB, The Honorable Richard M. Bilby, United States District Court Judge. QUESTIONS ANSWERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States District Court for the District of Arizona presented a certified question of law regarding the constitutionality of the Uniform Contribution Among Tortfeasors Act (Act), Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-2501 et seq. (1984), when applied to cases involving accidents that occur prior to the Act's effective date. Plaintiff injury victim's accident involving defendant alleged tortfeasor occurred before the Act took effect.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff injury victim brought the negligence action against defendant alleged tortfeasor arising from an accident which occurred before the effective date of the Uniform Contribution Among Tortfeasors Act (Act), Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-2501 et seq. (1984). Defendant raised the affirmative defense of contributory negligence. In answer to the certified question of the federal district court, the court first held that the Act was a constitutional enactment. The Act permissibly broadened the jury's discretion in negligence cases, in accordance with Ariz. Const. art. 18, § 5. Turning to the application of the Act to accidents that occurred before its effective date, the court noted that § 3 of the Act provided that the it governed in actions filed after that date. The court held that contributory negligence was a substantive legal right that could not be impaired once vested, and that vesting occurred when the case was filed. The court responded to the district court's certified question by stating that the Act was a constitutional enactment and was constitutionally applicable to cases filed after the Act's effective date that arose from accidents occurring before that date.


OUTCOME: The court answered in the affirmative the federal district court's certified question regarding the constitutionality of applying the Uniform Contribution Among Tortfeasors Act (Act) to cases that were filed after the Act's effective date but arose prior to that date. The substantive right to contributory negligence did not vest, and could not be impaired, until the action was filed.

Alvarado v. Industrial Comm'n


No. 18115-PR


Supreme Court of Arizona


148 Ariz. 561; 716 P.2d 18; 1986 Ariz. LEXIS 187



February 26, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Memorandum Decision of the Court of Appeals, Division One, filed February 5, 1985. George B. Marvel, Administrative Law Judge. Court of Appeals No. 1 CA-IC 2982. ICA Claims No. (2) 9/7-37-13 AND (4-10) 527-36-7285. Carrier Nos. (2) 69-36342, (4) AG-25630, (6) AU-48102, (7) AX-50695, (7A) 72-36017, (8) BD-18079, (9) 127CBHW07037P and (11) Unknown.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner widow sought review of a decision of the Arizona Court of Appeals, which affirmed the dismissal of the widow's claim in her action against respondents, the Arizona Industrial Commission (commission), employers, and insurers, to recover workers' compensation benefits for the death of her husband.


OVERVIEW: The widow's husband worked in the mining industry and was exposed to a variety of dusts and vapors his employment. Defendant broke his ankle while at work, and it was discovered at the hospital that he was suffering from a respiratory ailment. The husband filed a claim with commission and was awarded permanent total disability benefits based on the combination of his ankle injury and his respiratory condition. He received such benefits until his death, which occurred nine years after he was awarded permanent benefits. The widow filed a claimed for death benefits pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1046. The commission denied the claim. An administrative law judge (ALJ) found that the claim was time-barred under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1107(B)(3) because the husband died more than five years from the last day upon which he worked for the employer from which compensation was sought. The appellate court affirmed. The court reversed, concluding that § 23-1107(B)(3) abrogated the widow's rights under Ariz. Const. art. 18, § 8, which guaranteed compensation for a work-related injury or death, because it served to bar the widow's claim prior to the accrual of the claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court, which sustained the dismissal of the widow's claim for workers' compensation benefits, and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

State v. Correll


No. 6437


Supreme Court of Arizona


148 Ariz. 468; 715 P.2d 721; 1986 Ariz. LEXIS 175; 66 A.L.R.4th 383



January 28, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition denied by: Correll v. Ariz., 2002 U.S. LEXIS 6209 (U.S. Oct. 7, 2002).
Writ of habeas corpus denied Correll v. Stewart, 137 F.3d 1404, 1998 U.S. App. LEXIS 4037 (9th Cir. Ariz., 1998)
Petition denied by Correll v. Arizona, 537 U.S. 836, 123 S. Ct. 151, 154 L. Ed. 2d 55, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 6209 (2002)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Correll, 2011 Ariz. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1585 (2011)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Correll, 2014 Ariz. App. Unpub. LEXIS 841 (2014)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Correll v. Ryan, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 176135 (D. Ariz., Oct. 15, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. CR-141125, The Honorable J. D. Howe.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; SENTENCES AFFIRMED IN PART, MODIFIED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted defendant of three counts of first degree murder, one count of attempted first degree murder, four counts of kidnapping, one count of armed robbery, and one count of first degree burglary. Defendant was sentenced to death on each of the murder counts and life imprisonment on the other counts.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected defendant's contention that it was error to introduce evidence that defendant was someone other than Rick Watson. The court held that because defendant's identity was an issue, the trial court properly denied the motion to preclude mention of defendant's alias. The court rejected defendant's contention that the trial court erred in not declaring a mistrial after a witness mentioned finding marijuana on defendant, where the trial court had previously held that the marijuana evidence was inadmissible. The court held that although it was error for the marijuana to have been mentioned, the error did not materially influence the jury and did not merit mistrial or reversal. The court modified one of the death sentences to a sentence of life imprisonment, holding that findings that defendant killed, attempted to kill, or intended to kill one of the three victims was unsupported by the evidence. The court affirmed the other convictions and remaining sentences, holding that a total disregard for human life was clearly shown in the record and the only reasonably ascertainable motive for the murders was to cold-bloodedly eliminate any and all witness to a robbery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for first degree murder, attempted first degree murder, kidnapping, armed robbery, and first degree burglary. The court modified the sentence from death to life imprisonment for one count of the three counts of first degree murder, but affirmed the remaining sentences.

Goodyear Farms v. Avondale


No. 18275-PR


Supreme Court of Arizona


148 Ariz. 216; 714 P.2d 386; 1986 Ariz. LEXIS 168



January 13, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-438574, Court of Appeals No. 1 CA-CIV 7127, The Honorable Rudolph J. Gerber.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owners sought review of an opinion and decision of the Court of Appeals (Arizona) that reversed a summary judgment in favor of respondent city and declared the Arizona annexation statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 9-471, unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners sought review of the court of appeals opinion and decision that reversed a summary judgment in favor of the city and that declared the Arizona annexation statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 9-471, unconstitutional. The court decided on review that § 9-471(A)(1) did not violate the Equal Protection Clause of the United States Constitution and the Arizona Constitution by providing that only property owners were able to initiate annexation by the signing of annexation petitions. The court concluded that the petitioning process in § 9-471 was not analogous to voting, and therefore did not infringe on a fundamental right. The court held that the proper test to apply was the rational basis test. Accordingly, the opinion and decision of the court of appeals was vacated, and the ruling of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court ruled that the Arizona annexation statute was constitutional. The opinion and decision of the court of appeals that reversed a summary judgment in favor of the city and that declared the Arizona annexation statute unconstitutional was vacated. The ruling of the trial court that granted summary judgment in favor of the city was affirmed.

Anderson v. Industrial Comm'n


No. 18071-PR


Supreme Court of Arizona


147 Ariz. 456; 711 P.2d 595; 1985 Ariz. LEXIS 278



December 24, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Memorandum Decision of the Court of Appeals, Division One, filed January 17, 1985, approved as supplemented. Court of Appeals No. 1 CA-IC 3161; Industrial Commission No. 527-83-5192; Carrier No. 83-02078, Jerry C. Schmidt, Administrative Law Judge.



DISPOSITION: AWARD AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee appealed the judgment of the Court of Appeals, Division One (Arizona), which upheld the administrative law judge's (ALJ) decision in favor of respondents, Industrial Commission of Arizona (commission), employer, and insurance carrier. The court granted review to examine whether Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1024(A) required a finding that acceptance of compensation benefits was a waiver of the employee's constitutional tort remedy.


OVERVIEW: The employee tendered back his worker's compensation award and filed a tort action against the employer, a coemployee, and others. The employee attempted to withdraw his worker's compensation claim. The administrative law judge found that the employee had waived his tort remedy because he understood that he was accepting compensation. The appellate court affirmed the ALJ's decision. The appellate court also held that a waiver of the employee's common law tort remedies occurred even if the employee did not know of his alternative remedies or the consequences of his acceptance. The court granted review, approved the appellate court's decision, and affirmed the award. The court held that the intentional acceptance of compensation benefits was a statutory waiver of the employee's common law tort remedy against the employer. The waiver was effected by the act of accepting compensation because § 23-1024(A) stated that such acceptance was a waiver of common law remedies. The court found that the statutory waiver was permissible in the employee's case because the provisions of Ariz. Const. art. 18, § 6, which protected the employee's tort remedy in third-party claims, did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court approved the appellate court's decision, and affirmed the employee's worker's compensation award. The court held that the employee's acceptance of the award constituted a valid statutory waiver of his common law tort remedies. The court found that the constitutional tort remedy only applied to third-party claims.

State v. Cannon


No. 6093


Supreme Court of Arizona


148 Ariz. 72; 713 P.2d 273; 1985 Ariz. LEXIS 276



December 16, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County; The Honorable Thomas Meehan, Judge; Pima County Superior Court No. CR-09424.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE SET ASIDE; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which entered judgment of his conviction for armed robbery, dangerous nature and which sentenced defendant to life imprisonment without the possibility of release for 25 years, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604.01.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery, dangerous nature. Based upon a finding by the jury that defendant was on probation at the time of the robbery, the judge imposed an enhanced sentence of life imprisonment without the possibility of release pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604.01(A). Upon review the court affirmed defendant's conviction but set aside the sentence. The court held that defendant's confession was voluntary. The court further held that the decision by the trial judge to admit the tape-recorded confession to rebut proposed testimony by defendant that his confession was coerced and untruthful did not violate Ariz. R. Evid. 403, nor did it unconstitutionally hamper defendant's right to testify at trial. The court held that a contested jury instruction adequately served defendant's interest in presenting his defense, and was not so confusing as to warrant a reversal. The court set aside the sentence because the prior crime for which defendant had been on probation had not been designated a felony, and the enhancement provisions of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604.01(A) were only to be applied when the probation resulted from a conviction for a felony offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's armed robbery conviction and set aside defendant's sentence. The case was remanded for resentencing.

State v. Allie


No. 6233


Supreme Court of Arizona


147 Ariz. 320; 710 P.2d 430; 1985 Ariz. LEXIS 264



November 15, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County, The Honorable John G. Hawkins, Judge, Pima County Superior Court No. CR-11044.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction by the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) of burglary in the first degree and armed robbery and from the imposition of consecutive life sentences pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604.01.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of burglary in the first degree and armed robbery after he and an accomplice robbed a restaurant. Defendant was armed with a knife and he committed the crime while on parole. The life imprisonment sentences were to run consecutively to the sentence reimposed upon revocation of his probation pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604.01. The court affirmed the convictions and the sentence on appeal and held that (1) § 13-604.01, which mandated a life sentence for a person convicted of a felony involving the use of a deadly or dangerous instrument while on probation for a felony conviction, was not an ex post facto law; (2) the statute did not violate the concepts of equal protection because the legislature could rationally conclude that a felon who committed an armed offense recently after release from confinement for another felony was not rehabilitated; (3) the sentence was not cruel and unusual punishment when viewed in light of the gravity of the offense, the harshness of the penalty, the sentence imposed on others, and sentences imposed in other jurisdictions; (4) § 13-604.01 did not violate the Contract Clause; and (5) defendant waived his right to testify.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the constitutionality of the statute under which defendant was sentenced and affirmed defendant's conviction and sentences.

State v. Cocio


No. 6232


Supreme Court of Arizona


147 Ariz. 277; 709 P.2d 1336; 1985 Ariz. LEXIS 263



November 7, 1985

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County, No. CR-11014, The Honorable Lillian S. Fisher, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which convicted him on one count of manslaughter and one count of driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor. Defendant also sought review of the life sentence that the trial court imposed on him.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of manslaughter and driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor. The jury found the manslaughter charge to be dangerous and committed while defendant was on probation and also found that defendant had one prior conviction. Since defendant committed the dangerous manslaughter offense while he was on probation, the trial court sentenced defendant to life imprisonment pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604.01. On appeal, the court held that (1) the trial court did not err in failing to excuse a juror for cause; (2) the trial court did not err in instructing the jury on causation; (3) the mandatory life sentence imposed on the manslaughter charge did not violate the Eighth Amendment; (4) Ariz. State v. Leslie


No. 5806-2


Supreme Court of Arizona


147 Ariz. 38; 708 P.2d 719; 1985 Ariz. LEXIS 258



October 9, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County Number CR-118792 Honorable Ed W. Hughes, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) for first degree murder, alleging violations of U.S. Const. amend. IV, VI, claiming that he was prejudiced by the failure to instruct the jury on lost evidence, and arguing that he was improperly sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death. The court found that defendant's arrest was supported by probable cause where he matched the description of an attempted burglar in the sparsely populated area. The court held that 20 months between the grant of a new trial and the order for new trial did not constitute inexcusable delay where the state was justified in exercising its right to appeal, and defendant was not prejudiced from the period of incarceration and the absence of a witness whose testimony was read to the jury. The court reversed the conviction on grounds that defendant was entitled to a jury instruction on lost evidence because the state failed to remove and preserve alleged blood spots from the victim's car and made affirmative comments that they were blood. The court found that the comments evidenced the spots' materiality and the state created prejudice by using them to contradict defendant's claim that he never saw the victim. On remand, the court instructed the trial court under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-703 to give a detailed statement of whether and why it did not find mitigating factors for purposes of imposing the death penalty.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for first degree murder and death sentence was reversed.

State v. Rossi


No. 6326


Supreme Court of Arizona


146 Ariz. 359; 706 P.2d 371; 1985 Ariz. LEXIS 237



September 24, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

The Honorable Ed W. Hughes, Judge



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; SENTENCES AFFIRMED AS TO COUNTS I AND III; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING AS TO COUNT II


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for first-degree murder, first-degree burglary, and attempted first-degree murder, from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona). After a jury trial, the superior court sentenced defendant to death on the murder conviction, and terms of incarceration for the attempted first-degree murder and first-degree burglary convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was adjudged guilty of first-degree murder, attempted first-degree murder, and first degree burglary. The trial court sentenced defendant to death on the murder conviction, and terms of incarceration for the other convictions. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions, but vacated the death penalty. The court held that: (1) there was no abuse of discretion in denying defendant's request for a physical lineup seven months after the crime, and the photo lineup procedure was not suggestive; (2) defense counsel's performance was not deficient where the trial judge was fully apprised of the arguments in favor of mitigation; (3) the murder was committed in an especially cruel manner and in an especially heinous and depraved manner; and (4) the trial court did not understand the meaning and operation of the statutory scheme for finding the existence of mitigating circumstances and the evaluation and weighing of those circumstances. Because the trial judge used the wrong standard for determining and applying mitigating factors, the court vacated defendant's death sentence and remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder, attempted murder, and burglary. The court vacated the death sentence and remanded for resentencing on the first-degree murder charge.

Kriz v. Buckeye Petroleum Co.


No. 17914-CQ


Supreme Court of Arizona


145 Ariz. 374; 701 P.2d 1182; 1985 Ariz. LEXIS 220



July 2, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] QUESTIONS OF LAW CERTIFIED BY THE UNITED STATES DISTRICT COURT FOR THE DESTRICT OF ARIZONA

The Hon. Carl A. Muecke, United States District Court Judge

QUESTIONS ANSWERED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States District Court for the District of Arizona certified several questions of law concerning the proper interpretation of third party plaintiff securities dealer's complaint against third party defendant law firm, alleging violations of the Uniform Contribution Among Tortfeasors Act (UCATA), Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 12-2501 to 12-2509 (1984).


OVERVIEW: The securities dealer served as a selling agent for limited partnerships, and the law firm served as counsel for the limited partnerships. The limited partnerships filed an action against the securities dealer and the law firm in the district court under various federal securities laws and pendent state claims. The securities dealer filed a third party claim against the law firm and amended it to include the newly enacted UCATA. The district court certified questions of law to this court. The court held that the statutory scheme of the UCATA revealed the meaning of "actions" in § 3 as pertaining to only the underlying tort action. The court held that no contribution action could occur following the trial of a tort action unless the trier of fact had determined the relative degrees of fault of all the parties. Thus, if the tort action was tried under pre-UCATA law, no comparative fault finding could be made, and no contribution action was possible. Further, unless the tort action was filed on or after UCATA's effective date, UCATA would not apply.


OUTCOME: The court held that "actions", as used in a newly enacted statute, meant underlying tort actions and that joint tortfeasors could not make the law applicable to their actions by amending their contribution claims to after the effective date. The act created a separate and distinct cause of action for contribution that did not accrue until after one of several joint tortfeasors had paid more than its share of the common liability.

 

197 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Via


No. 6322


Supreme Court of Arizona


146 Ariz. 108; 704 P.2d 238; 1985 Ariz. LEXIS 217



June 12, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Via v. Arizona, 475 U.S. 1048, 106 S. Ct. 1268, 89 L. Ed. 2d 577, 1986 U.S. LEXIS 610 (1986)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Via v. Bramlett, 840 F.2d 22, 1988 U.S. App. LEXIS 2249 (9th Cir. Ariz., 1988)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. 137157

The Honorable Cheryl K. Hendrix, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted him of murder, theft of property, and fraudulent schemes. Among nine errors raised, defendant challenged the constitutionality of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3905 under which he was made to appear in a live lineup and he argued that it was error to refuse to sever the homicide count from those relating to charges of using the victim's credit card.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was convicted of murder, theft of property, and fraudulent schemes, challenged his conviction on the grounds that the statute authorizing his detention was unconstitutional. The victim, a real estate agent, was killed after meeting with a telephone caller who claimed to have land for sale. The body was found after another real estate agent informed police of a similar attempt to lure him to view some land by a man matching defendant's description. Pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3905, defendant was shaved and made to appear in a live lineup. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in failing to grant his motion to sever the trial of the murder and robbery charges from those charging fraud and theft. He also challenged various other rulings during voir dire and during his trial. Finding no error in the lower court's rulings, the appellate court affirmed the convictions because the challenged statute allowed for detention for no longer than three hours in order to obtain certain judicially authorized types of evidence. The appellate court also held that joinder of offenses was proper because all the crimes charged were part of a continuing series of events.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder, theft of property, and fraudulent schemes because the challenged statute satisfied the Fourth Amendment's litmus test of reasonableness. The court held that the offenses were properly joined and that a fair determination of defendant's guilt or innocence was not jeopardized by the lower court's refusal to sever.

 

198 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bracy


No. 5809


Supreme Court of Arizona


145 Ariz. 520; 703 P.2d 464; 1985 Ariz. LEXIS 215



June 10, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at State v. Hooper, 145 Ariz. 538, 703 P.2d 482, 1985 Ariz. LEXIS 216 (Ariz., 1985)
Writ of certiorari denied Bracy v. Arizona, 474 U.S. 1110, 106 S. Ct. 898, 88 L. Ed. 2d 932, 1986 U.S. LEXIS 1271 (1986)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

The Honorable Cecil B. Patterson, Jr. Judge
State v. Cruz, 137 Ariz. 541, 672 P.2d 470, 1983 Ariz. LEXIS 248 (Ariz., 1983)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted defendant of conspiracy to commit first degree murder, two counts of first degree murder, attempted first degree murder, three counts of kidnapping, three counts of armed robbery, and first degree burglary. Defendant was sentenced to death for each count of first degree murder and to approximately 140 years for the other crimes.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of first degree murder and other criminal offenses and was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed, alleging that the state engaged in continuous misconduct and that he was denied a fair trial. The alleged misconduct involved nondisclosure of evidence and misconduct exclusive of nondisclosure of evidence, including the state's comment regarding pretrial identification in its opening argument and improper trial publicity. The court held that while the state's conduct was improper, there was no evidence that defendant had been prejudiced because the trial court instructed the jury to disregard the statement and because the trial judge questioned all the jurors regarding the article. The court also rejected defendant's argument that the death penalty was unconstitutional because the jury took no part in the sentencing determination and because Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-703 gave the trial court no guidance as to what the mitigating factors were and how to weigh them against aggravating circumstances. The court affirmed, holding that pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4035, it had examined the entire record for fundamental error and found none.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions of conspiracy to commit first degree murder, two counts of first degree murder, attempted first degree murder, three counts of kidnapping, three counts of armed robbery, and first degree burglary. The court examined the record for fundamental error and affirmed the sentences imposed, holding that the suppressed evidence would not have affected the outcome of the trial.

 

199 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hooper


No. 5810


Supreme Court of Arizona


145 Ariz. 538; 703 P.2d 482; 1985 Ariz. LEXIS 216



June 10, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Hooper v. Arizona, 474 U.S. 1073, 106 S. Ct. 834, 88 L. Ed. 2d 805, 1986 U.S. LEXIS 2523, 54 U.S.L.W. 3462 (1986)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Claim dismissed by, Motion denied by Hooper v. Schriro, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 14516 (D. Ariz., Mar. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

The Honorable Cecil B. Patterson, Jr. Judge
State v. Bracy, 145 Ariz. 520, 703 P.2d 464, 1985 Ariz. LEXIS 215 (Ariz., 1985)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) for conspiracy to commit one count of first degree murder, two counts of first degree murder, one count of attempted first degree murder, three counts of kidnapping, three counts of armed robbery, and one count of first-degree burglary and sentence of death, life imprisonment, and 140 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced for his participation in contract murders. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by requiring that defendant be shackled during the trial because of the nature of the crimes and the fact that extensive precautions were taken to assure the jury would not see the restraints. The line-up in which defendant was identified by the witness was not unduly suggestive because there was nothing to single out defendant. Even if it was unduly suggestive, the identification was admissible because although it was unduly suggestive because the witness had the opportunity to see defendant, she was at a high level of attention, and she had a high level of certainty at trial. The trial court properly limited expert testimony as to the identification of defendant because the court chose not to apply a new rule allowing such testimony retroactively. Additional safeguards were present at trial to minimize the possibility of a miscarriage of justice. Defendant was not allowed to withdraw his waiver of a right to a jury trial on his prior convictions because the waiver was voluntary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for conspiracy to commit murder, first degree murder, attempted first degree murder, kidnapping, armed robbery, and burglary.

 

200 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Ford v. Industrial Comm'n


No. 17585-PR


Supreme Court of Arizona


145 Ariz. 509; 703 P.2d 453; 1985 Ariz. LEXIS 210



June 5, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied August 20, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: INDUSTRIAL COMMISSION

Peter B. Chickering, Administrative Law Judge

Decision of the Court of Appeals, Division One, filed April 19, 1984 approved in part, vacated in part.



DISPOSITION: Award - AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant filed a petition for review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals, Division One (Arizona), which affirmed the administrative law judge's (ALJ) determination. The ALJ had ruled in favor of respondents, industrial commission, employer, and insurance carrier, and had denied all compensation to the claimant under the Arizona Workers' Compensation Act (Act), Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-901 et seq.


OVERVIEW: After a hearing on the claimant's request for benefits, the ALJ denied all compensation. Although the claimant had sought benefits under the Act's general provisions, the ALJ held that the claim had to be considered under Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 23-901(12)(c), 23-901.01, the occupational disease provisions. The ALJ determined that the testimony did not establish the six compensability requirements of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-901.01. The court of appeals affirmed the determination. On appeal, the court vacated the judgment of the court of appeals insofar as it held that mere aggravation of a pre-existing disease was not compensable in an occupational disease setting. The court otherwise affirmed the judgment because it was within the ALJ's prerogative to deem the testimony of the doctor who consulted on the claimant's condition more credible than the testimony of the claimant's physician. The consulting doctor stated that he did not believe work exposure had aggravated the claimant's condition as compared to simply triggering symptomatology. Thus, the ALJ's finding that the claimant did not prove a connection between work exposure and his condition was supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated to the extent that it held that mere aggravation of a pre-existing disease was not compensable in an occupational disease setting. The judgment was otherwise affirmed in the action by the claimant challenging the ALJ's determination in favor of the industrial commission, the employer, and the insurance carrier, which denied him all compensation.
